<Author>calilregit
<Content>Horror Show I am an experienced traveler. I travel for business and pleasure. We take two vacations a year as a family. Those vacations are for a period of seven to 20 days each. My wife and I have used Tripadvisor for years. She has posted in the past but I have only used the site for my edification and am writing today for the first time. Our current travel experience has prompted me to write.I almost always look askance at postings of a terrible experience at a hotel that has a high Tripadvisor rating assuming it was an aberration. Alas, we are in the throws of such an experience at the Hotel 1898 in Barcelona, Spain. We love Barcelona. This is our second trip to the city. On our first trip, we had a wonderful experience. Great sites. Great people. I purchased one of my favorite pieces of original art from an artist in Barcelona which hangs in the entrance to our home. Our second trip to Barcelona has been a horror show. We came to the city for two days prior to a cruise. Our flight from Boston was delayed 10 hours but we slept on the flight to Paris before our connection to Barcelona. We looked forward to the Hotel 1898 as an oasis from the downside of travel. Alas, Hotel 1898 was anything but an oasis. My wife lost her passport. We assumed she lost it in the Barcelona airport but her recollection is that she had it in the hotel room. We take responsponsibility for not putting our cash and passports in the safe in our room. The passport is missing along with 300 Euros. It is a curious amount to be missing because it was three 100 euro bills that were taken from a larger sum of money and not all of the money was taken. We have taken the position that we lost the passport and have not complained to the hotel. We did ask them for their recommendation on what to do and they recommended we report the lost passport at the police station. They also told us the police would give us a report that would allow us to travel. I tipped the gentleman behind the desk 20 euro for his assistance. We did as advised and the police were very accommodating. We were told it will be up to the cruise line as to whether they let us board.We chalked the downside of our trip up to the adage: ---- happens and were ready to put the incident behind us for the rest of the evening. Alas, that's when we ran into a Barcelona we had not seen before. In the lobby of the hotel is an oriental restaurant, La Xina. We looked forward to a relaxing dinner in the hotel. It was 10pm and we were told by the restaurant to return at 11pm for seating. Upon our return we were told a table was not ready and that we should go up to the bar and they would let us know when a table was ready. The bar consists of an oak runner around an open kitchen. Four bottles of Moet and some wine were stacked in a plastic crate filled with ice. There were no more than eight bottles of alcohol on the counter. It looked more like a bar you would see at a house party. I waited patiently while the young man made three frozen margaritas. Just before he was done another man that worked at the restaraunt came up from downstairs with five young women in tow. He stepped front of me and spoke to the bartender who nodded in return. Upon finishing the margaritas and passing them to a waiter the bartender looked past me to the young women to take their order. I politely said, Excuse me. Without missing a beat, he told me he knew I was waiting but that he was told to wait on the women next. I asked the ma卯tre d if the restaurant was affiliated with the hotel or unaffiliated (I did not bother to complain). He told me it was unaffiliated. One can not give one's business to an establishment that could be so outwardly rude. Our family went for pizza down the street. When I travel I maintain low expectations and normally appreciate the courtesies extended to me and my family as guest saway from home. The Hotel 1898, and its unaffiliated restaurant, failed at meeting even the minimum standards.

<Author>summertimes11
<Content>A negative part of our trip I just looked up this hotel, suprised to still see it is #3 in Barcelona. I have been meaning to write a review on this hotel because of the fact that staying here made me dislike Barcelona (hotels really can affect your overall view of a place, unfortunately). I usually trust trip advisor, and I did when I booked this hotel. The hotel rooms are nice, the roof deck/pool is great, and the hotel is beautiful. It is also in a great location. The problem with the hotel is the staff. The staff on our initial 2 days there were horrible, unhelpful, and never smiled (particularly the front desk staff). On our final day there, after much complaining, we managed to find some helpful staff and wished they had been that nice the entire time. A great hotel should never have mean, unfriendly, and unhelpful staff. The best part of our trip was when we actually left the hotel and stayed elsewhere!

<Author>travellingsquacks
<Content>Won't stay anywhere else!! My wife and I just stayed at H1898 for eight nights, from 21 to 30 Nov 2008. Given the length of stay, we had initially thought of trying two different hotels (the other hotel we considered was the Meridien next door), but we are now glad that we stayed the entire period at H1898. We had a privilege room on the third floor overlooking the Ramblas. There were two windows, a large one opening out onto the Ramblas, and a smaller side window looking at the Meridien. The choice was made after we had inspected a superior room and a deluxe room (with a terrace) for comparison. The privilege room appealed because of its large size, high ceiling, separate sitting area with full length sofa, and above all else, its fantastic bathroom. The bath room was not only large and luxurious (in a classy green marble), but really clever in design, because it had twin vanities (facing each other) OUTSIDE of the main bath room, which housed a bath tub, WC, bidet and a generous glass enclosed shower stall with a rain shower. This room was definitely a five star rather than four, on account of this bath room and the size. The window facing the Ramblas brought life and light into the room, the sounds of pedestrians, street vendors, entertainers, and even clinking of cutlery in near by restaurants, wafted in along with the cool autumn air every evening. We felt pretty much part of the street scene even as we sat in the comfort of the sofa sipping sangria.Its location on the Ramblas is simply superb. Although there are a multitude of hotels all along the strip, this particular corner is literally a few steps from the Plaza Catalunya (transport hub for the airport bus, tourist bus, metro, tourist information), and also the location of Carrefour right next door means grocery shopping is a cinch. A daily trip there for fresh fruits and bottled water became a routine for us. Via the Ramblas, almost all the major sights are walking distance including the GOthic quarter, the Palau Musica, the Palau Guell, the Columbus monument, the Gaudi masterpierces of Casa Batllo and Casa Milla, and the main shopping street on Paseig de Gracia. The hotel is also a few steps from the La Boqueria Market, which means you can eat the freshest produce and sea food the city has to offer every day. The excellent Bar Boqueria in the market itself is great value for money. After we found it, we ate brunch and dinner there almost every day. Forget about the tourist trap restaurants touting tapas sets along the main street.Finally two features make H1898 truly magical, instead of merely excellent. The roof terrace with its really classy outdoor furniture, which offer a panoramic view in three directions (the fourth being blocked by the Meridien), best enjoyed in the early morning and late evening. Many other reviews have raved about the terrace so no further elaboration is needed. However, it is the indoor pool which captured my imagination and which I really want to draw attention to. It is in the basement, and while not big (about 9m x 4m), the cavernous design with serial roof arches and gothic stone claddings on the wall, together with special lighting effects, and haunting music make swimming here a surreal experience. On one end, there is a large back-lit black and white picture of padi fields carved into a cliff which makes one think of Bali. An early morning swim will definitely invigorate and give a great start to the day. The adjoining changing rooms come complete with towels and toiletries so you don't need to bring anything from your room. Strangely, it was always empty on each of the occasions I used it. Perhaps it should remain a well kept secret.Overall, despite going with already very high expectations from reading all the past reviews, the reality managed to surpass our imagination. The staff are helpful and responsive when approached, but are otherwise discreet rather than proactive, The only one gripe I have is the hotel could not provide an umbrella on a rainy day. Given the room rates, I think it is fair to expect this provision in every room since it is not a standard item in most travellers' luggage.

<Author>autumngirlCork
<Content>100% in every way! My daughter and I stayed at the Hotel 1898 for 3 nights last weekend. We stayed in one of the privilege rooms overlooking the rambla. It was sound-proof which was greatly appreciated except for the occasional tolling of the cathedral's bells. The room was extremely comfortable, the beds were fabulous and flat screen tv showed english channels. Bathroom was spacious with power shower and generous towels. We enjoyed our reflexology in the spa on the sunday evening and the staff were friendly and helpful. The spa was a wonderful haven of peace after spending the day in the busy streets of the city. Our stay in this hotel was one of the most pleasant and enjoyable of any hotels we have stayed in the past. I would recommend Hotel 1898 to anyone and everyone. The location is perfect as it is so central to all the districts and the maremagnum is also accessible at the end of the rambla. When I visit Barcelona again I will definitely stay here, wouldnt dream of going anywhere else after such a relaxing stay in Hotel 1898. Thank You!

<Author>travelsny
<Content>Great find in Barcelona We stayed in this hotel prior to our tour of Spain based on the reviews it had received on multiple web sites and travel magazines. The building is the former headquarters of a import/export (tobacco?) corporation and actually looks like a former bank that's been extensively renovated into a chic boutique hotel. It's location on the Ramblas is very convenient and is across the street from the Meridien. You can actually see the Meridien from the lobby which is decorated much like a gentlemen's private/yacht club i.e., dark wood, model sailboats, black and white photos, and club furniture. Service is quite professional and efficient since many business persons use this place. The rooms are quite spacious, especially the corner units, and decorated with Pottery Barn/Crate and Barrel type furniture. The bathrooms are very comfortable with granite/stone tiles, large tubs and showers, and good quality soaps/shampoo. Although we didn't have a chance to use it there is a spa and pool which appears to be quite nice on the web site of the hotel. If you want something light the tapas restaurant in the hotel is great--much less olive oily than the traditional fare found in many restaurants. And, for those who can't do without Starbucks, there is a branch in the hotel itself where you can get a reasonably priced coffee and baked goods for breakfast. This place is actually much nicer, larger, and cheaper than the Meridien where we also stayed during the trip--don't bother with the bigger name hotel, this is the place to stay!

<Author>james76manchester
<Content>brilliant hotel we stayed here for my girlfriend's 30th birthday in september despite other hotels being rated more highly on trip-advisor at the time as we liked the look of the decor and the fact it had a rooftop pool and garden.we had a deluxe room which looked away from las ramblas and are located on the higher floors, making it quiet. it also had a terace which was great to relax on.the room was on the small side but the terrace gave you extra space. it was beautifully decorated and very stylish. the same can be said of the lobby and the rooftop bar and pool area, which was brilliant for relaxing in after the bustle of barcelona. the prices for food at the rooftop bar were not cheap as people have commented, but it was fairly quiet when we stayed and we were able to ask the barman to see if we could order food from the room service menu instead and have it brought up to the rooftop. he asked for us and it was no problem, so that made it much more reaonable. the pool was too cold for swimming in but the chance to lie in the sun more than made up for that. they also let us hang out there on the day we checked out as we didn't leave barcelona until the evening but we were able to keep using the facilites all day. the indoor pool was excellent as well.also the staff were helpful when we were trying to book restaurants and in general they were very polite. as noted previously they didn't carry our bags up to the room for us upon arrival, but personally i don't mind that. i certainly didn't have any problem with them as previous reviwers have commented.overall this is one of the nicest hotels i have stayed in and i would definitely stay there again. it is expensive but if you can afford it the extra cash for the deluxe room is worth the price.

<Author>SORCEL
<Content>Great stay at 1898 We have just come back from a 3-day stay at the 1898 Hotel in Barcelona. We drove over from France and had no difficulty in finding the hotel. We arrived with a flat tire and the staff were extremely helpful in getting it fixed. The staff were ever so friendly and spoke excellent English. The hotel is well located. In the same building there is a Starbucks and there are lots of small restuarants (not too pricely and with a good selection) to be found in and around the street Carrer de les Sitges which is just a block further up (but be warned they don't start eating dinner before 20:30 in Barcelona). Our room was small - but pleasant (classic). It was kept very clean and tidy, twice a day by housekeeping staff. The beds were comfortabel and you get to choose between a large choice of pillows. We were also very pleased with the large flat screen TV which was easy to view from bed. The bathroom was also small - but clean and covered in beautiful green marble.The hotel has an historical feel but all the facilities are modern. The entrance from La Rambla is amazing. We will not hesitate on choosing this hotel on our next trip to Barcelona.

<Author>mullet_rock
<Content>Fantastic location! If there's one thing I regret about my stay in Hotel 1898, it's the fact that I only stayed for a night here. I loved this hotel -- from its facilities, the room, the service and the location.Location -- It's along Las Ramblas, so there is a lot of activity going on right when you step outside the hotel. It is a touristy area, so for some it may not be your cup of tea, but it is conveniently located beside MANY shops, cafes and most of all, the La Boqueria (a large public market quite famous in Barcelona. Make sure to go here if you're a foodie). You'll never get bored (shopping and lot of street performers) or hungry here. There's a McDonalds and KFC a few minutes walk away from the hotel, so if you're starting to miss the fast food, you can always go there. Room -- Immaculately clean. The design was very nice. My room was navy blue and white, very classy. Quite spacious for one person, really. They were quite generous with the amenities as well. There's a cool room feature that sort of sets the overall lighting of your room depending on your mood / activity -- for watching TV, for entertaining visitors, sleeping, etc. :)Staff / Service -- Professional and accommodating. Although I really didn't get to interact with them that much except for check in/out and when I asked for an electrical adaptor. But all in all, they were alright.Price -- Got this hotel because of an error made by the travel agent in my booking, so this was a pleasant mistake. But I would say it is still good value for the money. Facilities -- I haven't had the chance to use the facilities, but from what I have seen of the spa and the pool, I would like to go back and try them sometime. Food - Nothing remarkable. Don't expect an eye-popping spread, but it's alright. Overall - I love the hotel for the location, primarily. The fact that the other factors such as the room and staff were great is just icing on the cake.

<Author>JMBINCA
<Content>Good for first time visitors to Barcelona My partner and I stayed at the Hotel 1898 for 5 nights on our trip through Southern Europe. All in all, a good experience for the following reasons:1. The location is right in the heart of Barcelona's main sights. The hotel is right on the upper part of La Rambla, which is the main street that divides the Gothic Quarter and the Raval districts--the two areas that are probably of most interest to tourists. You are within walking distance of the Cathedral, the Picasso Museum, the waterfront and the central marketplace, plus many good restaurants. You are also within easy walking distance of most of Gaudi's most famous works, which are generally in the neighborbood called Eixample--just north of the Gothic quarter and Raval. You will probably want to take the metro to Gaudi's Sagrada Familia, however, as it would be a long walk.It is also less than a block away from Barcelona's highly efficient and cheap subway system, so you can also have quick access to other districts in no time. La Rambla is known for being pretty raucous, even into the wee hours of the night. But Hotel 1898 is apparently well insulated, as we could not hear any street noise at all. Granted, we had a room on one of the inner courtyards of the hotel (which we would recommend, as there isn't a great view from the rooms on La Rambla), but, even with the windows open, we didn't hear a thing. If you would prefer a location that is not right on La Rambla (e.g. quieter), we would recommend the hotels in the lower part of the district called Eixample, right on the other side of the Catalunya square from La Rambla. These are still great locations, but without the craziness of being right on La Rambla.2. Great breakfast. Our room rate included breakfast, and we would recommend you ask for the same. The breakfast is served daily from 7am to 11am. It is buffet style/all-you-can-eat, and has everything you could want. Fresh fruit, cereals, eggs, breakfast meats, waffles, pastries, vegetables, fresh juices and even diet food.It is served in the main restaurant on the second floor, but, if you book a day in advance, you can also eat on the rooftop with views of Barcelona. 3. Nicely decorated rooms. The hotel is in the former building of the Phillipines tobacco company, and, although fully renovated, they have decided to keep the decorations consistent with the Filipino/tobacco theme. Lots of beautiful wood (floors, mouldings), marble and hallways lined with pictures from old Filipino tobacco plantations. The rooms tend to be done in green and white, red and white or brown and white stripes...very hip and modern, with still a nod to the past.4. The rooms have luxurious fittings and amenities. The bed, in particular, was awesome. It was even larger than a California King, and very comfortable. Down pillows and down comforter (which we didn't use because it was warm). They also have one of the better air conditioning systems I've experienced in Europe. And you can set it just the way you want it. And they have pre-set lighting scenarios you can choose from with the touch of a button, depending on your mood. For instance, they have one for romantic night lighting and one for reading. It was a nice touch.Plus, they had free wireless access that was very quick and easy to use.5. Rates were reasonable for the luxuriousness of the hotel. The hotel is at the higher end of the offerings (although there are even more luxurious offerings), and the rates we paid seemed like they were quite a bit less than other comparable hotels. We paid 225 Euros per night for the smallest size room, and similar hotels were charging 300-350 Euros for similarly sized rooms. So we felt like we got a good deal.OK, so there were a few things that we didn't like, which is why we didn't give it a 5:1. The shower was a bit of a disaster. It has three nozzles...a rain shower, a hand shower and the main tub faucet. There are three handles to control each of these, and each of these handles had sub-handles. I dare you to figure them out easily. We had to have the concierge come explain it to us, and even then it was really difficult to get it to work properly. My sense is that many people have complained about the complications of the shower, as they have a directions card in the bathroom to tell you how to use it...but I followed them exactly and couldn't get it to work.Plus, there was no cold water in the shower. The coolest you could get it was luke warm. It was hot in Barcelona, so we occasionally wanted a cold shower and couldn't get one. When we called to ask about this, they said they had never heard of anyone wanting a cold shower, so they didn't provide it as an option.2. They didn't have a concierge that we could find, and we could have used one to give us advice and help book events. So, we had to do this on our own, which did create hassles every now and then. The front desk staff tries to answer your questions, but they aren't as knowledgeable about the city and sights as one would hope.3. Not a big deal, but the lighting system I mentioned above does have one fatal flaw. Like many European hotels, you have to leave your card key in the main light switch for it to work. If you forget to leave it in there and have to turn a light on in the middle of the night, watch out...because, when you put the card key in, it automatically turns all the lights on, waking up anyone who is trying to sleep. One of those instances where they've over-engineered the system, in my opinion.4. The cheapest rooms are tiny. There is little room to walk around the bed and little storage space. You're constantly tripping over your luggage. They do have larger rooms (for a premium, of course), which we would recommend you take. Again, their rates are reasonable by Barcelona standards, so you can give back part of your savings to get a larger room. It will make the experience better.So, all in all, we really enjoyed our experience here and would recommend the hotel, particularly to first time visitors of Barcelona. But, if we were to go to Barcelona again, we would probably opt to stay in one of the hotels in the lower Eixample. Now that we know the city, we don't need to be right in the heart of La Rambla.

<Author>cheeseburger23
<Content>One of my favorite hotels ever My husband and I just returned from a stay at Hotel 1898. We couldn't have been happier with this hotel, and often had difficulty prying ourselves away from its confines to experience Barcelona. Some of the other reviews I read complained of poor service. We didn't experience anything like this. Everybody we met was extremely friendly and helpful. It wasn't like Four Seasons service where everybody is asking you every thirty seconds if you're okay, but if you express a need, it's seen to immediately.We booked a terrace room which will go down as one of my favorite hotel rooms of all time. We had an enormous private terrace, almost as large as the room, with beautiful plants, two spacious loungers, and a large table. We ate several meals out here and spent a lot of time relaxing. It faced a side street so noise from La Rambla was minimal.The room itself was decorated in black and white with rich wood floors. A/C was extremely powerful and worked brilliantly. TV was great with many more English channels than most European hotels. Enormous closet with plenty of storage space to unpack completely. Free Wi-Fi. The only complaint we had about the room is that our King bed was quite literally two LARGE single beds. Not bound together in the traditional manner, but actually on rollers and easily separated. This is fairly common in Europe and didn't really bother us. Bathroom was nicely appointed and spotlessly clean. Fresh robes and slippers every day. Nice toiletries and included shaving and dental kits automatically. Mini-bar was a bit sparse, but we stored things that we bought in the Starbucks downstairs in there and they didn't seem to mind.Location-wise, it can't be beat. It's right on Las Ramblas, and a two minute walk to the nearest Metro stop. Restaurants, shops, and conveniences abound. The shopping district is pretty much across the street. La Bocaqueria, the most amazing food market in Europe, is three minutes walk. For a quick fix, there is a Starbucks in the same building as the hotel.Food in the hotel was very good. Definitely above average. Room service was delivered within 20 minutes every time and always hot and delicious. We tried the buffet breakfast and were very pleased with it. Lots of little luxuries like champagne were made available. We ate in the main restaurant one night and LOVED our food. Service was also good, and they let us take our time. We ate on the rooftop restaurant another night and besides the shockingly high price of drinks we had an immensely beautiful dinner. How can you beat the view from the rooftop cafe as the sun sets over all of Barcelona? It was a memorable experience.Pools were fantastic. The rooftop pool was small, but refreshing, and the lounge areas on the rooftop are just too much fun to relax on. We went for a rooftop swim as the sun was going down our last evening in Barcelona, and it was simultaneously fun and romantic. The pool down by the Spa is really fun-looking. The gym was small, but we weren't there to work-out. We didn't try any of the spa services, unfortunately.Overall, we found this hotel to be a really good fit for us. We are relaxed people who don't like to make a fuss, but we also like our luxuries when we're on vacation. This hotel epitomized that relaxed luxury, and combined it with jaw-dropping views and location. If we're lucky enough to go back to Barcelona, we won't dream of staying anywhere else.

<Author>Mokita
<Content>Hotel 1898--beautiful but let down by uninterested staff We just returned from five days in Barcelona staying at Hotel 1898. I really wanted to like this hotel and the facilities are beautiful but the staff lets the place down. Upon arrival, we were struggling to get out of a cab with all of our luggage, our eighteen month old son and his pushchair--being dropped off into the madness of the Ramblas--and the doorman at Hotel 1898 simply stood and watched us. Did not lift a finger to help until we pulled all of our stuff together and struggled over to the door. That should have been a sign.Check in was okay and the room was lovely, if a bit small for a so-called superior, especially when you add the baby cot. My husband went down to reception to ask for matches and they did not have any. That's okay but when he asked where he could get some or purchase a lighter, they simply shrugged and turned away. When I needed a cab, which I did every day since I was on business, I went out to the doorman who told me I had to go ask at the desk--despite the fact that there were four cabs lined up in front of the hotel with no passengers! And when I did ask at the desk, I would have to wait ten minutes or more while these empty cabs idled outside. What's THAT about?We had a function to go to on Saturday night and asked for an iron to iron my husband's shirt. We were told none was available for guests but that we could use their laundry service to get it pressed, which would cost us money, of course. Very very naughty from a supposed five star hotetl The prices are high, yes, particularly on the rooftop bar where a drink sets you back 12 euros or more. And none of the receipts--for room service, drinks, anything--let you add a tip. So, if no one is working for tips, it's no wonder the services is so shoddy! We kept loose euros on us to tip the deserving ones such as the rooftop bar servers. The rooftop is lovely but maybe instead of staying here, you should just visit it.There were many more small slights--room service order errors (because the person taking the order could not understand English), LOUD rooms--bring your earplugs, LOUD housekeeping staff--all if it adding up to make this more of a three star hotel than a five star hotel. It is beautiful but the service really lets it down. And since we were paying 225-275 euros a night, it should have been better.Will find somewhere else to stay next time I'm in Barcelona.

<Author>DLM-F
<Content>Loved the 1898 Stayed at the 1898 for a week for our wedding anniversary and loved it. We had a 'superior' room in the red and white colour scheme (331) which was immaculately clean and had plenty of room. Nice touches included the robes and slippers and the fact they always replaced the soap - maybe petty but I've stayed in some '5 star' places that expect you to use one tiny piece of soap for your whole stay. Plus toothbrush and shaving kits as standard in bathrooms - no having to ask reception if you'd forgotten something.The location is ideal for exploring Barcelona - I don't know how someone can describe the location as 'awful' - umm if you don't want to stay on La Rambla - then don't, but it's on a major tourist central road - I'm not sure what they expected . The room was lovely and quiet considering where it was located. We didn't eat in the hotel as it did seem a little expensive for what was on offer and there are plenty of cafes nearby - there's a Starbucks next door for those craving a caffeine fix and a number of small supermercados nearby for picking up water/drinks for cheaper than the mini bar. I will definitely stay at the 1898 for our next Barcelona trip - in fact I can't wait.

This was truly a 5 star experience. I shall be booking there on our next trip for sure. I cannot recommend this hotel to anyone, because I felt it was majorly overpriced for what you get. Majorly disappointed and not sure why this hotel is number 1 in Barcelona????!!!!!!!!!!

<Author>Shliben
<Content>Smart hotel, a little let down by precise and unemotional service We came to the 1898 for our 25th Wedding Anniversary and made the choice based on the position of the hotel and the roof pool and bar (and the generally positive reviews). Overall not disappointed,but there are few minor issues that mark the hotel down a little. First the positives:Great position, really easy to get to from the airport - the bus stops around 500 metres away - and central for everything, right next to La Rambla. The roof pool (for dipping) and the bar are really great; they made a great Negroni - very strong. The drinks are expensive but you are paying for the fact you are on a roof with really comfortable seats and a good view. Food is also pricey and not hugely original. One evening we ordered a selection of meats for 鈧?3 and received a plate of one type of ham! Staff on the roof are very willing but service is a bit slow if there are a lot of people. Bedroom was large (Privilege Room) with a fantastically comfortable bed; room was well sound proofed with efficient A/C. Huge choice of pillows if important to you.Free newspaper (laser printed) every day.We didn't use the spa in the basement but it looked good if a little small.Now the minor niggles, which did not detract from our stay but should be ironed out based on the prices they charge:Free tea is offered every day in the lobby between 5 and 7 pm. The lobby and bar lack atmosphere (everyone is on the roof!). There was no one around to serve the tea and when the barman eventually was found we were not offered a choice of tea (there were 2 types) but the tea was poured and it was pretty awful!One of the bathroom taps kept falling off and we were only supplied 1 small piece of soap (both these issues were rectified the day the hotel was notified) The A/C control is inside the main cupboard: It's very hard to read the control and if any staff member needs to get at it they have to go into your cupboard where all your stuff is stored - not a great piece of planning.No biscuits in the room with the coffee - a bit penny pinching.We did not eat breakfast at the hotel (v. pricey) but there are loads of places outside - even a Starbucks in the hotel building if you like their coffee!The staff at the main desk are polite and efficient but as has been mentioned by other reviewers they do what is necessary and no more. That little extra touch is missingOverall we would stay again in one of their standard rooms and spend all moments at the hotel on the roof, which is the highlight.One other thing; Eat at Alkimia restaurant, Industria 79 behind La Sagrada Familia. Fantastic chef - and yet again precise, cool service - must be a Barcelona trait.

<Author>baer_ke
<Content>Fantastic oasis in the most central location This hotel is located very central at all day long lively La Rambla, close to Plaza Catalunya. Therefore one is always in the middle of everything and can reach shopping, sightseeing, city tour busses, plenty of restaurants and even the waterfront in short walking distance. Travelling to the airport can be done very easily via the airport bus (costs ca. 4 EUR pp) which goes to Plaza Catalunya - then ca. 5 min. walk to the hotel.The hotel itself is fantastic. Great service, extremely clean (it seems they are cleening all day long) and it offers a fantastic roof terrace with pool and bar. The terrace is the perfect place to escape a bit from the vibrating city life - you can just relax at the pool or lay in one of the roof terrace couches and enjoy some drinks or food. The pool bar is open late night and they also offer breakfast up there but one has to pre-order that the day before. - That seemed a bit odd and they were not flexible if you just wanted to take the breakfast there in the morning without preordering. Another advice: as you stay so central there is always cabs going along outside the hotel you don't need to order that via the hotel - some cab drivers charge up to 6.20 EUR for coming to the hotel after being called - even though they just drive around the corner ... So, just stop a cab at the street, works all the time.

<Content>A beautiful retreat in the heart of Barcelona!!! Having just returned from our honeymoon in Barcelona I felt I had to write a review of the 1898. As with any hotel booking there is always some trepidation, especially for such a special occasion, but the 1898 fulfilled all the criteria on our list. <Author>BrazAustralia
<Content>Classy  The title of this review is a bit of a give away...Position- spot on- right in the guts of La Rambla...initial perspective, lobby etc, very classy, expensively done, very stylish. The reception people were a tad cool I thought, not overly burdened with a service ethic. We arrived around 1pm, and were told that check in was at 3, and felt that they didn't really try and help us in what we might do for 2 hours. They weren't rude or anything ,just didn't really seem to care too much. Anyway, our friends booked into their room- a normal one with a view over a alley way/stairwell thing, and we went to our superior room- v expensive at 420 Euros, but very well appointed, lovely big king size bed, superb pillows, and a sun terrace. good for entertaining. All a bit small for the $$$ however- comparing it to the room we had in a Paris hotel afterwards.We were on the 5th floor, out the back, overlooking a plaza that got a bit noisy later in the days. Faciities are very good, the gym/ pool complex in the basement was very groovy, as was the bar/ pool area on the roof- warning- don't try and dive in the pool, it is tiny and only knee deep, really there for true dipping as opposed to anything else.Yes, drinks are expensive, but the 360 degree view is superb. The service levels stayed the same over the 3 nights we were there- cool, standoffish- they don't help people in off the street with their luggage for example- they stand back and wait for you to come to them! Didn't eat there, too many choices outside.All in all, as I've said above. I think it was expensive for what we got, I think you may as well just get an ordinary room, a fair bit cheaper. I wouldn't stay there again, as much to do with the overall attitude as much as the value- they are linked of course.

<Author>ce04dje
<Content>Don't look elsewhere go to the Hotel 1898 After much searching for an hotel in Barcelona, on the strength of reviews for the Hotel 1898 I booked a 3 night stay here - I was not disappointed.The hotel location is fantastic - directly on to the Ramblas, and is very well located for shops, nightlife, harbour etc. Despite its central location, the hotel itself was very quiet. I asked for a quiet room and was given a room on the 6th floor, which was on a side street (so did not face the Ramblas). There was no noice from outside or inside the hotel.The room itself (a superior room) was very nicely furbished, a good size bathroom, and a good size room. No complaints about the room at all. Other revies referred to a balcony. There was no balcony, only a large window that opened. (NB The suites on the 5th floor below us had their own private terraces, and I noted some had their own private pool).The rooftop terrace and pool were brilliant. A great way to chill out and relax in the heart of the City.We dined on the rooftop one evening and the food was very good. No complaints about the breakfast - plenty of choice.The hotel itself is not cheap, but I would regard it as value for money, on the basis you get what you pay for. You have to remember this is regarded as a Luxury hotel. We had cocktails on the rooftop terrace which were 10 euros each - the same price as a beer on the Ramblas !I would recommend this hotel to anyone wishing to go to Barcelona (and have done so), but not on a tight budget. If I was returning to Barcelona, it would be my first choice of hotel.

<Author>paaluz
<Content>Nice hotel, need to iron out some faults The Hotel 1898 is located in the former buildings of the Philippines Tobacco agency of Spain, a trading company. This makes for a truly nice and genuine old building, where the insides have been ripped out and redone completely. Absolutely everything inside is new, including the newly carved out parking garage.We arrived to check in without any problems, after first having some quarrel with the GPS. The street La Rambla is not a valid GPS destination for this hotel, after calling the hotel we were told the street address is Pintor Fortyun 1, and the GPS guided us to the front door.The location is on the main tourist street in BCN, apart from the scores of cheap-flight tourists hanging around the location can't be more perfect in BCN.After check in we ordered parking for the car a bit pricey at 23 鈧?per night. But the garage is right under the hotel, amazing for such an old building and I was guided in by the bellhop. The room is probably too small for its price category, but very tall and nicely done. Very clean, and always magically cleaned when we were out. The A/C was found inside the closet not difficult to find but a bit difficult to read the screen. After shivering through the night with an overzealous A/C I decided to read the manual and discovered how to run it proper.Room was quiet, apart from some low hallway noise. Not a nuisance.There's plenty of channels on the TV, but not all of them were as according to the manual. Nice to have Fox Series to watch in the evening after the spa.We did not feel the 20 鈧?breakfast was a good enough value to eat in the hotel.On the roof is one of the major assets of this hotel, a smallish pool and a very nice bar. The pool is good for a dip in the heat and there is several beds along the rooftop. Ample amounts of towels and a complimentary bathrobe makes the lack of changing area near the pool a non-issue.In the bar, there's no a lot of perfection, in spit of the staff effort. They are courteous and friendly, but not very professional. Also, the drinks are very off on the recipe, like the strawberry daiquiri. Nice selection of cheeses on a plate along with a bottle of good red wine is a much better bet in the not very comfortable large divans. The spa in floor -1 is nice, with a warm and comfortable spa pool. Steam sauna is still out of order, and the Finnish sauna was not hot enough at 70 degrees Celsius and low humidity.At the business centre, there's the usual Americans hogging the computers chatting along with home base in Kentucky or where ever but fortunately there is enough of them to go around. I had to print, sign and fax a contract in the evening and none of these actions were an issue. WiFi in the room was very slow and needed a login and password from the desk to function.All in all, this is a 4/5 because there's some issues that need to be corrected. They have an almost perfect building and location but partly fail on details and prices. This does not mean that the hotel should be avoided, however.

<Author>BoomerBanker
<Content>Great hotel and location My wife and I really enjoyed this hotel. I have stayed in Barcelona before on business trips and this time I was at the Hilton for a meeting before moving to the 1898 for three nights. I was not at all disappointed; we were in a standard room facing the courtyard so no view but it was very quiet considering you are right in the middle of all the action on the Rambla. Staff was highly courteous and allowed us to check in at about noon which was terrific. Needless to say, with the current exchange rate of about 1.65 dollars to the Euro, it is not cheap (about $450 a night) but it's one of the nicer hotels I've stayed in, and I've been to quite a few. The rooftop view is great, just be careful as a few drinks will set you back at about $18 a pop. The location is spectacular... I have heard the Meridian across the street is also very nice at about the same price or higher, and the 1898 has a lot of history to the building. The mood lighting as described in other reviews is nice. Bathrooms very pleasant. Internet access is free in the business center on the second floor (called Floor 1). Not much nightlife in the bar, mainly due to the fact that the weather was so great that everyone wanted to be outside. Have a great time!

<Author>E_Hemingway
<Content>Close but not perfect There is certainly no complaints about room size or style. Not sure what room the reviewer had that said they couldn't swing a mouse but ours was big by European standards. A lot of storage and a large bath for two with a brilliant rain shower. The bed was a true queen / king size (not two pushed together) and the style of it was very modern and chic, without being two cold and souless. The turn down service supplied fresh towels if you had used the ones supplied in the morning during the day. This was a first in my experience.The roof top pool isn't olympic size, or one you would do laps in. But it has 360 degree views and is great on a hot summers evening. The euro habit that used to be confined to Germans of putting towles on pool chairs is alive and well here. I didn't spend much time at the pool but one morning I noticed two chairs were reserved for over two hours. There are not many of these chairs so if you can't beat them join them and get up there early then go have breakfast.The roof top bar is wel appointed and has great views. The furniture consists of large lounges and cushions. Very pricey though. It also attracts outsiders so I would assume gets busy in peak summer.The only reason I didn't give 5 was the staff were just so indifferent and the bar prices over the top. The staff at the roof top bar didn't want to know you and were certainly not friendly. I don't really care about service but on this trip had stayed at a place just before this one that had brilliant personal service which really made this place look even worse than it probably was.Also, I could be wrong, but it didn't seem to have air conditioning in the rooms? It wasn't overly hot so not an issue, but would be in August. I couldn't se any controls or vents.

<Content>impeccable Lovely hotel in the heart of Barcelona. We stayed at Hotel 1898 in June 2008 for 2 nights. We really enjoyed our stay at the hotel but the rooms are a little small, especially at 拢350 a night. We had a terrace so that helped, otherwise we would have felt too squashed in. The bathroom was lovely and with me being 6'2 the bath was ample. As for the rest of the hotel, the spa in the basement was nice, but the water in the pool was extremely cold. Almost to the point of shivering, the steam room was not working either! We found that it would have been nicer if someone from the hotel had shown us around first as it was a little off putting just walking round free roam. The roof top bar/pool was ok. The bar is extremely expensive, 拢15.00 for a gin and tonic. The pool on the roof is very small, the photos on the hotel website make the pool out to be bigger than it actually is, also there is no where to change on the roof so if you are wanting a quick dip in the pool, forget about it. You would have to walk back through the hotel dripping wet. Also we couldn't find any dry towels on the roof on 2 occasions. We didn't have breakfast in the hotel as for 鈧?0 it seemed expensive. Plus the hotel has a door into the Starbucks next door so we just went there {be warned though that in Barcelona none of the Starbucks Menus had a translation so unless you are fluent in spanish/catalan you might just have to guess}.We had drinks in the reception area of the hotel, but again very expensive and the quality was nothing special. They had very little choice if you didn't drink alcohol, which is the norm in Barcelona from what we found. We found that the hotel staff didn't really speak to us much, even though they had door staff and reception staff. This was a little off putting. We were able to check in at 12 o'clock which was nice. The music system in the room didn't work at all and the TV was almost unwatchable, very fuzzy! for 拢350 a night you would expect these things to work. The pillows and bed were lovely though. Very gay friendly in the hotel, we had no issues with that. If anyone has any questions feel free to contact me x

<Author>Blondii
<Content>Expensive, but top notch quality. Finally, a hotel worth its star rating. The interior of this hotel was every bit as nice as the exterior. It exuded understated elegance. The location was excellent right in the center of everything on Las Ramblas. The staff was very friendly and helpful too. The reception, bar, and sitting areas were very classy with leather seating, club chairs, and 1930's style of decorating. The business center was outstanding with 4 computers with free internet access, leather furniture, and a conference table. Again, very classy. The rooftop bar and pool area was great. The spa and pool area in the basement was top notch. I had the silk feet massage and it was wonderful, but too short. The breakfast buffet was pretty good. You could special order eggs, which was nice. It wasn't worth 20 euros, but typical pricing for western Europe.We booked a superior room. It was very clean and quite lovely with quality features: king size bed with a selection of pillow types, plasma TV, wood floors, light dimming switches, room safe, robes, slippers, etc. The bathroom was in marble with a nice rainfall showerhead. Although not huge, the bathroom was above average compared to other 4 and 5 stars we have stayed at. There were several complaints on tripadvisor about room noise, but our room faced the side street and was very quiet.We payed an average of 315 euros per night which is very expensive by American standards. We have stayed at less expensive 4 and 5 star hotels in other major European cities only to feel disappointed in the end. We were very pleased with our selection this time.

<Author>AnnieBrando
<Content>Probably the best hotel we ever stayed. I have booked this hotel for my husband's special birthday treat, so my expectations were very high, I wanted everything to be perfect. And to be frank, it probably was. Although quite pricey, the location is fantastic, the hotel is very modern and furbished in elegant, understated style. We stayed in the standard room, which was not large, but still a decent size and airy, certainly not pokey or dinky. I was worried about the noise from La Rambla, so asked for quiet room at the back when booking and our room (No 404) fitted the bill perfectly. In fact, we got really good night's sleep (the bed was large and very comfortable) and did not wake up before 9 am. We skipped the breakfast, at 20 euros, it's expensive and you can eat like a king at plenty of cafes in the neighbourhood or at the Bouqeria market. The rooftop pool and terrace are just fantastic, great to unwind in late afternoon to catch the last of sunshine before going out in the evening. The same goes for the grotto pool, sauna and the gym in the cellar. The reception staff was very helpful, they secured us a last minute reservation at Hisop on Saturday night. I cannot fault the cleaning or other services either. The toiletries in the bahroom also contained complimentary toothpaste and shaving kit, which was a nice touch, now when you have all these flight hand luggage restrictions on liquids and sharp objects. If you can afford it, this is the ultimate choice.

<Author>scbrown
<Content>Perfect location to explore barcelona My wife and I had the opportunity to visit Barcelona recently without the children, and so I wanted to book a quality hotel that would not disappoint. I chose the hotel 1898 mainly based upon tripadvisor reviews and we thought the hotel was absolutely fabulous.The location is as near perfect as you could find being on La Rambla. It is convenient to the Plaza de Catalunya which has the departure point for the two tourist bus companies as well as shops and restaurants. La Rambla is always extremely busy but the hotel althought located on this street is like an oasis from the bussle of the throngs of people. Indeed when relaxing in the lobby of the hotel it is hard to imagine that outside it is so busy.There were two things we particularily enjoyed at the hotel. The first was the rooftop terrace. People in their reviews constantly refer to this terrace but it really is that good. The views were outstanding and it is so relaxing. The second thing we enjoyed was the spa in the basement: what a lovely way to enjoy an hour or indeed two. The spa was very clean and tidy and in the pool area the jacuzzi beds and water jets were so much fun.We booked a superior room and my first impression was that it was a little bit smaller than I had imagined. However the quality of the room was evident to see in both the fittings and style of the room. The bed was very wide and there was a choice of four types of pillow. The room had a sound system that gave a choice of continuous music to whatever type you found relaxing as well as a lighting system that allowed to select for different moods/requirements which I found quite good.The reception staff were helpful in chosing restaurants and had books showing the decor and menus of several. We chose one called Barkeno and if you like fish I can highly recommend it . It is also within walking distance of the hotel.The hotel is not inexpensive but if you are looking for a good 4 star hotel then in this location it is well worth the expense. I certainly would stay at this hotel again.

<Author>DepDawg
<Content>Great location, roof pool and stylish rooms - poor service I chose 1898 on the basis on TripAdvisor reviews and as usual was not disappointed - the location, just off Las Ramblas near Placa Catalunya is central and excellent. The hotel is quirky and full of history but styled recently very similar to the Hotel du Vin chain in the UK (good). The hotel is clean and well appointed and rooms are (for city centre) well sized with air conditioning in room, free internet, and good bathroom.The staff I met did slightly let down the hotel. I realise they are full all year, deal with tourists and transient business travellers every minute of every day, but regardless, they are in the service business and the couldn't care less disinterested attitude to any question (neither complaints or compliments) in both English or Spanish, was the only thing that let this otherwise excellent hotel down.Didn't try any hotel food at all - this is Barcelona and there are great restaurants (try Barceloneta for fish or Comer莽 24 for tapas). Would I go back - yes - so that says it all.

<Author>chitownguy1
<Content>Overall two thumbs up for Hotel 1898 Hotel 1898 is a unique, trendy property in the heart of the action, Las Ramblas.We booked the hotel for three nights starting Monday April 28th. We didn鈥檛 arrive until 4:15 PM and so the 3 pm check-in time was a non-issue. We had reserved a superior room and we were given Room 445, facing Las Ramblas. - Ok, so for those that have commented on the noise factor in past posts and for those who may be concerned about this 鈥?it is a real issue if you have a room facing Las Ramblas. When we checked in, I specifically asked if the room faced Las Ramblas and was told yes, to be fair. I asked for a different room facing another street but was told there were none available. The noise was not a factor on Monday evening or Tuesday evening 鈥?keep in mind we were out until 2 AM or so ourselves and once we hit the pillow we immediately passed out! So, no worries there. On our last evening, we were in bed quite early by Barcelona standards 鈥?11 PM 鈥揳nd by now it was Wed of course. There was constant noise all night long and admittedly it was pretty loud at times 鈥?seemed like there was an actual rave happening down on the street below! My fianc茅 and I laughed it off in the morning 鈥?it wouldn鈥檛 keep us from staying there again 鈥?for reference we are thirty-somethings who aren鈥檛 terribly conservative but don鈥檛 party until dawn anymore either. Another point on the noise 鈥?the Metro runs underneath the hotel (at least it feels like it must) 鈥?every 15 to 30 minutes you can feel the train passing by鈥eels like a 1 or 2 on the Richter scale actually. Did we sleep through that every night? Absolutely. Did you wonder what the hell it was the first or second time it happened? You bet. On to the wonderful traits of Hotel 1898鈥he lobby and rooms are of spectacular design and feel. The designer did a great job of combining modern amenities with an Asian twist (building housed the old Filipino tobacco company in case you didn鈥檛 know). The lobby is amazing, complete with a sitting area and bar. The dark hardwood floors and green/black color scheme is really cool. Room 445 is a Superior Room and provided considerable more space than a standard room (we peaked into a standard room being cleaned as we walked by). There were two twin beds pushed together to form a double which was a little annoying. Another negative was no iron in the room. As an American I think we just needed to get used to this concept, that's all. However like Casa Fuster we checked through Travelocity and assumed there were irons in the room - not the case. Anyway, I digress.I know a couple of other reviews talked about things being stolen from the room - a non-issue with us although we used the in-room safe religiously. The bathroom was very nice with rainfall showerhead, bidet and toiletries. My fiance liked the full length mirror against the bathroom door as well as mirrors above the bathroom sink and behind you on the back wall. Altogether we were very pleased with the room. It had a nice layout and was very clean and stylish. The rooftop terrace is awesome 鈥?a pool slightly larger than that of Casa Fuster鈥檚 (where we stayed prior to the Hotel 1898) and a bar on the rooftop with posh, comfortable seating all around. Definitely a huge plus.The basement spa and exercise facility are also quite nice. Compared to Casa Fuster this was far superior. The exercise room had 2 treadmills, 2 bikes, a stairmaster and a weight bench with some dumbbells. The basement pool was more of a spa pool with a couple of jaccuzzi-type massage chairs and a few shower-type waterfalls. There is a sauna and a steam room as well as two showers. One can also book massage although we opted not to do so. We certainly enjoyed the basement pool on two different occasions in the afternoon after a long day of walking. The service of the staff was definitely above average. However, keep in mind we had just come from the Casa Fuster where service was far superior. Hotel 1898 staff just weren't quite as overly accomodating is all, although we didn't find fault with anyone at all. As I posted in my Casa Fuster review, it was more of a 'we provide the info, you do the work type of scenario. The staff did book a taxi for a 6:30 AM departure upon checkout without issue. Location, location, location. Noise comments aside, one cannot beat the location of Hotel 1898 if being in the thick of the action is your thing. The hotel is right across the street from Le Meridien and, although we didn't go inside and although Le Meridien has recently been renovated, Hotel 1898 certainly appears to have trumped the Le Meridien. More importantly, the hotel is 5 minutes or less from La Boqueria, 5 mins from the Barri Gottic (if that), and perhaps 10-15 minutes to Born. We loved this about the hotel. By the way, we never felt the least bit unsafe leaving/returning to the hotel. It was a sanctuary from all the action going on just outside the front and side doors. We would definitely stay at the Hotel 1898 again. A very cool place.

<Author>hersoton
<Content>Fantastic hotel Stayed in this hotel in Sept 07, choosing it after seeing it was located right on Las Ramblas, and No1 on Trip Advisor for Barcelona. Never got round to reviewing it, partly because it was just as good as everyone said and there was nothing to add. But now I see it has slipped to No3 - probably because other people who loved it thought the same! So I have to set the records straight and say just how fab it is!!!Stayed here for two nights at the beginning of a cruise starting from Barcelona, and for one night at the end. The rooms were great and exceptionally well equipped. Luxury bathrobe, cute 1898 monogrammed slippers, and lovely toiletries come as standard. Also welcome was a kettle and tea making facilities (so rare in Europe), as well as very useful fridge, safe etc. Beds were huge and very comfy, and the bathroom with state of the art shower was also fab. The lobby with its huge seating area and ground floor bar are a great place to relax, and lovely and cool in contrast to the heat of Las Ramblas outside. But the highlight has to be the open air roof terrace with fantastic views of Barcelona, rooftop pool (small but great for cooling off), roof top bar and a huge range of sunbeds, al fresco four poster 'beds' (yes really!), sofas etc. A stunning place to relax with a drink, or a book, or even take a snooze - day, evening or night. There is also a basement indoor spa which we only looked at briefly, but would be a great place to relax during a winter stay. The dining room also looked inviting although we didn't sample its fare, and breakfast looked great but wasn't cheap (so if you are a breakfast fan look for a breakfast inclusive package).We also loved Las Ramblas - don't expect the chic of Paris or you will be disappointed. But for buzz and atmosphere its hard to beat - a huge range of bars and resturants, street entertainers and market stalls leading down to the port. Nearby squares are inviting, with yet more resturants and some great shops and tapas bars - the Calamari seemed to be consistently fantastic wherever we tried it. And the huge glasses of Sangria have to be seen to be believed!! On the waterfront (just at the bottom of Las Ramblas, turn left when you reach the water and walk for about ten minutes) there are some fabulous seafood resturants, and a great bar situated on a boat which is a stunning place for an early evening drink. From here its only fifteen minutes walk or so to the beach; the close proximity of beach and city is one of many things that make Barcelona so unique. Here there are another huge range of resturants to choose from - our favourite undoubtedly the Carpe Diem Lounge Bar - yet more al fresco 'beds' where you can sit and lounge with your drink and even eat dinner - totally surreal!! And from here its only another ten minutes or so walk to the Olympic Marina with a huge range of resturants and nightclubs - and a taxi rank to get back to the hotel if your feet aren't up for the walk home! Other things we loved included Gaudi Park - amazing architecture and fabulous views over the city. A bit of a walk from the nearest underground stop but well worth it. We also loved the sensational Fountain of Montjuic that does a fabulous 'Sound and Light' show around 9pm every Thursday to Sunday evening in Summer (Fri and Sat in Winter) - nearest Metro stop Placa Espanya. And finally no visit to Barcelona would be compete without visiting the Sagardia Familia and taking the lift to the top. This unfinished cathederal is simply unique - a truly amazing place. Its difficult to describe just why its so good; you just have to go there and see!!! Queues for the lift were long when we were there, but worth every minute of the wait.Overall I can only highly recommend both Barcelona and Hotel 1898. Only one disadvantage. When you say to a taxi driver at the Airport or wherever you would like to go to 'Hotel Eighteen Ninety Eight' they look at you completely blankly - since of course it woud be said completely differently in Spanish!! So unless your Spanish is excellent, have a pen and a piece of paper to hand - as soon as you write down 1898 they get it straight away!!!

<Author>nickmichael
<Content>Nice hotel, well-situated We spent three nights at H1898. We wanted a top-end establishment in the heart of the touristy part of the city, and we picked the 1898, well, to be honest, because of the tripadvisor reviews - I think it was no. 1 in popularity at the time of booking! The reception was slightly disappointing - in spite of my having given my credit card details when booking, the clerk insisted on taking a photocopy of the card, something I have never encountered before. The room (we took a 'superior' room) was superbly furnished (it must have cost a bomb to kit out!), with mahogany furniture, exotic parquet flooring and a gorgeous all-marble bathroom. Everything was spanking new, and not a sign of shabbiness anywhere. I particularly liked the lighting 'modules', whereby you can choose a programme such as 'Welcome', 'Ambience', Read', or 'Night'; I wish I had installed such modules when recently building our house, but had never heard of them or imagined them before. At night the room was quite noisy. This didn't bother us as we wanted a room right on La Rambla, and sleep well through noise; but the window was ill-fitting, and it sounded as though it was open all the time. The hotel could well do a bit of work on soundproofing, which could be far more effective. The bed was very comfortable, but I could have done with sheets and blankets rather than duvets, which are far too hot (I often end up taking the duvet out and sleeping under its cover only). The bathroom was luxurious as I have said, but why only one tiny cake of soap? It looks mean amidst all the luxury. The bath taps were complicated to work out: there were three of them, all with different functions, and the porter could have given an explanation when he brought the bags up. The service at reception was excellent (although we only asked for restaurant bookings in town a couple of times). Otherwise the reception staff were perfectly helpful and friendly.The spa was delightful (although I was hoping for a jacuzzi temperature!). We didn't check the roof terrace and pool as it was far too cold. Breakfast was fine, but perhaps a trifle dear. We had the small breakfast: coffee, tea or chocolate with ready-made salami sandwiches, or croissants and pastries, for 鈧?. The large breakfast (strangely called 'continental' - which for me is a limited meal) looked excellent, but very expensive (鈧?0 I think) and we didn't want to fill ourselves up before lunch.I was disappointed by the fact that there was nowhere (apart from outside on the roof) that I could smoke. Most hotels have a smoking room or you can smoke in the bar, but I was banished to a sleazy bar in the Pla莽a Reial to indulge my naughty habit (I can hear righteous non-smokers cheering). But there seems to be no reason why the beautiful and unused marble hall giving on to the side-entrance (La Rambla entrance) should not be set aside for smokers. The situation is perfect for the tourist, being smack in La Rambla, and almost everything you want is within not unreasonable walking distance (Park Gu毛ll apart).The price is perfectly normal and reasonable for what the hotel is - no arguments there.All in all a good experience, and tripadvisor's reviewers were absolutely right. We would certainly stay here again.

<Content>A perfect hotel for room only Stayed four nights here and loved the location ,comfort and cleanliness of this hotel.We booked a superior room and it was quite a good size.I think all the superior rooms overlook the Rambles,and even though the windows have excellent double glazing it can be a bit noisey.The housekeeping was excellent,and the sheets were changed daily and towels twice daily.The first morning we ordered a continental breakfast to our room and it was quite good .The next morning it came it seemed as if it had been prepared the night before.We ate out the next morning(and there are plenty of coffee shops etc.minutes from the hotel)On the morning before we came home we had the restuarant breakfast at 21 euros.For a cold breakfast it was okay but the bacon and scrambled egg were just on cold trays.My husband ordered an omlette and it was more like a burnt fried egg! <Author>boatmusdir
<Content>Great location poor food noisy rooms The hotel has a terrific location, and the building and decor are superb. Our room was rather small, and almost windowless (just a very small window at one end) and whilst the bathroom was excellent, the room itself attracted all the corridor noise - especially tiresome when (after our 12 hour flight) the domestic staff started loudly and energetically cleaning the rooms at 7.15 am. The staff were pleasant and helpful, but the breakfast, although abundant, was poorly maintained - hot items eg.scrambled egs, bacon etc. were left to go cold, and bread was left to go stale. Worse, room service delivered exceptionally poor food - salad that had obviously sat for hours, fish that was old and oily, stale rolls, and an inedible hamburger. The cuisine of this hotel is distinctly poor, and more attention should be paid to sound proofing the rooms.

<Author>dougfromnj
<Content>Amazing Experience, Perfect Honeymoon! Absolutely wonderful stay. They upgraded us to a room with a deck b/c it was our honeymoon to start which we very much appreciated. The room was wonderful, very modern with a beautiful deck where we spent a lot of time. The decor was very modern, more like the Omni than the Ritz. The location in Las Ramblas is PERFECT. Right in the middle so you can either walk up to Placa Catalunya, walk across to the Gothic Quarter, or walk down to the water. We love to walk so this was the best location as we walked to many places from here such as the Picasso Museum and La Padrera.Our routine was to run around the city, come back and sunbathe on the gorgeous roof deck, then take a dip in the roof pool or go to the basement where they have an awesome grotto like pool. The roof was even better at night to grab a drink with some ambient lighting and views of the city. Front desk was helpful with food recommendations and how to get places. Everything about the hotel was beautiful. Very nice staff. I hope to go back to Barcelona one day, and if I do, I can't imagine staying anywhere else.

<Author>DanielleM
<Content>Excellent except the front desk The hotel 1898 is ideally located on the Ramblas. It has been beautifully refurbished. Rooms are nice, privilege rooms are superb. Everything is 4 stars level except the front desk. During our both stays in this hotel, we were disappointed by the low level and the lack of friendliness of the staff at the front desk. The service you are expecting from a 4 stars level is nil. Examples : You need tickets for the Opera (Liceu) : it is at walking distance, do it yourself. Ordering a taxi 2 hours ahead for the dinner on 31st December : take the metro, it is not possible. Ask for a small hour late check out time on the first January : impossible. It is rather hostel style than 4* level. Pity because it is the only weak point. Fortunately very unusual in this category of hotels in Barcelona.

<Author>cmm3
<Content>the best value for the money in BCN I spent 4 nights in Barcelona following ThanksGiving a few weeks ago. Two of those were spent at the Hotel 1898 and I have to say that I would have spent my entire stay but they did not have availability for all four nights 鈥?unless of course you count the Colonial Suite for 1500 Euro a night, which is 鈥?regretfully 鈥?outside my budget for Barcelona.I also spent two nights at the Casa Fuster which was also very nice, but much more expensive than the 1898. In the end, although I liked the Casa Fuster better than the 1898, I really cannot fault the later for very much. Although the hotel truly falls short of a 5-star property, it is probably the best value in Barcelona 鈥?euro for euro 鈥?hands down.I had a Superior room which was large, comfortable, and contained a number of great amenities. I also really enjoyed the 鈥渕aritime鈥?themed decore that was echoed throughout the hotel. Instead of cheesy hotel art there where nautical charts, maps, and old photographs aThere was a fairly large marble bathroom with a full bathtub. It鈥檚 definitely not the most luxurious bathroom I have seen, but it did the job and was certainly spacious enough for one person. Although there were two sinks, you really had to squeeze to accommodate the second person. Most noteworthy was the 鈥渁utomated鈥?lighting system. I have seen this many times before, at other hotels but I was really impressed with it at the 1898. One button turns all the lights on, one turns them all off, one keeps the bathroom lights on and a small 鈥渘ightlight鈥?and there are modes for TV watching, reading, and more. Other hotels attempt to do this but I always find myself manually turning on various lamps, unplugging others, and generally cannot seem to make use of the automated lighting features. I also got to make use of the indoor pool which I absolutely loved. I never made it to the gym section 鈥?which was small but stocked with a few treadmills, elliptical machines, bikes and light free-wieghts. While I was swimming I noticed a number of people using the equipment 鈥?so people do actually get good use out of the gym. This whole section looked like it had just completed renovation and looked brand new, swimming in the indoor pool as the temperature outside dropped a few degrees every day was a dream. I did not make it to the rooftop pool but it looks fantastic from the other trip advisor pictures. There is a bar up there in the summertime, but it was closed at the end of November when I was staying there.The breakfast was also standard 4-star fare. I did notice a number of exotic fruits like dragon fruit and passion fruit which I wasn鈥檛 expecting to find but for 19 Euro a person I can鈥檛 say it was any better or worse than your standard over-priced hotel continental breakfast. I wouldn鈥檛 pay for the breakfast again. One evening after I was tired from a full day of sight seeing and wanting to rest before heading out for drinks, I decided to eat dinner in the main restaurant of the hotel rather than head out. I walked in at 8:45 and there was not a single person there. Just 2 or 3 bored waiters. Needless to say, I walked right out and went to the restaurant next door to the hotel 鈥?I think it was called 鈥?11.鈥?I wish I would have avoided the hotel鈥檚 restaurant b/c seeing it empty like that left me with a disappointed feeling about the hotel in general. Although the 1898 offers so much for the money, I don鈥檛 believe it really could be a truly deluxe 5-star property. Although everything was very nice, it was obvious where a few liberties had been taking in order to save money and be able to offer the value. The furnishings had this low-cost feel to them, almost like what IKEA would offer if they went the maritime traditional look. Sure, it looks great in a catalog and on a website, and at the end of the day it gets the job done, but there are certainly better options (for more money, of course). My biggest complaint however were the towels in the bathroom. Although there were many of them and the bath towels were extremely large, they felt like towels you are given at the local gym when working out. Either they had been washed way too much or I have been spending too much time at the Four Seasons and have gotten used to soft towels. I don鈥檛 know. How hard could it be to provide soft towels? And speaking of the Four Seasons, I thought the mattress could have been a bit softer, but I find that firmer (and slimmer) mattresses are the norm in Europe and so this was not unexpected.I should say that the choice of pillows was a very nice touch thought I did not have an opportunity to take advantage of it.Although I have gone on and nit-picked a little above and I have decided not to give the 1898 5-out-of-5, I want everyone to know that the above negatives are totally minor. I would stay at the 1898 again a thousand times! It is the perfect choice for a hotel on the Ramblas. It is so close to Placa Catalunya and a perfect starting point from which to enjoy the city. There is even a Starbuck鈥檚 attached to the lobby for all those who are homesick but want to avoid McDonalds et al. 鈥?but watch out: At a worse than $1.50/Euro exchange rate on the street, those white chocolate mochas will cost you dearly 鈥?as will everything else. The old adage 鈥測ou get what you pay for鈥?is certainly true, if you want a truly deluxe experience, 225 Euro per night for a superior room will simply not get you there. Instead you get an experience that approximates the 5-star deluxe hotel which for most 鈥?and at those fantastic prices, is more than enough.

<Author>woody1975
<Content>Luxury and tranquility at Hotel 1898 Hotel 1898 is a luxury boutique hotel where attention to detail leaves a lot for its rivals to desire. Reception staff are warm, friendly and helpful. Our classic room was spacious and modern, a real delight. The pillow option is wonderful (try the memory foam option for ultimate comfort) and the ability to change the room lighting with the clever dimmer options is a joy. Rooms are cleaned twice daily, beds turned down in the evening and chocolates left by your bedside. Our room faced the courtyard, a peaceful oasis away from the rustle of Las Ramblas. Ladies, one tip bring your own hairdryer, the hotel suppliers a hairdryer that is too heavy, especially if you have long hair! We didn't opt for the hotel breakfast, there is plenty of choice, with an abundance of local eateries within walking distance (try Vienna for snacks)and Starbucks on the corner. Two tips, flag the taxi on Las Ramblas, taxi's ordered on your behalf incur a 5 euro charge on the meter and eat later than you normally would. The Spanish tend to eat from 9pm onwards. For a fab restaurant with views over the city try [-], its really breathtaking. Really enjoyed my stay but at 199 euro a night plus 7% VAT I expect to! Try it you won't regret it.

<Author>mikh43
<Content>Outstanding hotel Hotel 1898 is outstanding and even after decades of business and leisure travel qualifies for one of my personal 'top ten'. The decor is an exciting blend of old (it's the 1898-built HQ of a colonial tobacco company) and new - sensitively and stylishly brought right into the 21st century with a blend of Scandinavian style and top notch interior decoration with great attention to detail. The rooms have almost every possible facility - and we stayed in the cheapest (interior view rooms are actually best if you want a quiet night). Plasma screen TV - even in-room tea/coffee making facilities - rare in Europe outside the UK. Rooftop heated outdoor pool with a view to die for over the city. Indoor cellar pool, spa and sauna - all free. Service immaculate - friendly, helpful and unfailingly courteous. Position ideal for the tourist - right on Las Ramblas and a very short walk from Plaza Catalunya (metro, airport buses, tourist info and tour buses). I can't comment on the food as we ate out - spoilt for choice in Barcelona. This is not the cheapest hotel - but by no means the most expensive and great value for money if you want a little treat. I am usually super-critical but can find little to fault here - and I have absolutely no connection of any kind with the hotel!

<Author>91Chris
<Content>Brilliant location, terrific style I booked 1898 for a 3 night stay with my teenage daughter. This is the first time I have used trip advisor to find a hotel and will definately use it again. I have never written a review before and would not do so had I not been a)grateful to all the other reviewers who advised 1898 and b)been so impressed with the hotel.The location of 1898 is brilliant. It is right on La Rambla so within walking distance of many of the sights. It is also within easy walking distance of Placa de Catalunya which is where public transport departs for the airport.The hotel has a terrific mixture of old and new style. It is housed in the old Phillipines Tobacco Company building yet has been modernised with a contemporary feel. Plenty of old polished wood and leather armchairs, mixed with black, white and red furnishings. Lots of nice touches such as heated mirrors in the bathroom, different automatic light settings etc. Quite unlike anywhere else I have stayed. (We even remarked on the style of the black and white stone stairs when we walked to our room rather than taking the lift!)The rooftop pool is heated so we were swimming in it in October! And the view from the terrace is fantastic (shame it is not open longer hours in the winter...we would have liked to have seen the view late at night as well). There is also an indoor pool and fitness area in the vault downstairs.This is described as a luxury hotel which it certainly is. However, I thought it was extremely good value. I would have expected to pay at least 50% more for something similar (if it existed) in England. Even more than that in London.Overall we were very impressed with the hotel and would definately go back.
