<Author>BlueBananaSkin
<Content>Style and luxury on the Ramblas I have just come back from 4 nights at the 1898. I relied on the comments and ratings from Tripadvisor and they were spot on: The superior room is easily big enough for all but (possibly ?) the North American market, which does after all like things really BIG. The hotel bed was one of the most comfortable I have ever slept on. Normally I long to be back in my own bed, but this one was just perfectly comfortable - not too hard and not too soft. Very dark curtains means you can sleep all morning and not realise it! (yes, I did...)Dimming room lighting: bit of a gimmick, but very nice touch once you get used to itLinen was crisp and heavy cotton, and changed daily. Towels were changed twice daily (dont go here if you are an eco-warrior!)Shower and bath taps: I noted the comments on TA: its really not rocket science - there is one dial for temperature, one for shower/bath tap, and one for small shower head on sep pipe. There is no need for further instructions, IMHONoise: had a room overlooking ramblas (room 444). Could hear some noise through double glazing (occasional police siren, some traffic) but never enough to disturb or prevent sleep. Benefits of overlooking ramblas outweigh noise problem. If you're a VERY light sleeper, go for internal room. Spa and pools: superb. Dark cellar pool was atmospheric, roof terrace pool superb location with view of city. Roof terrace probably comes into its own in the summer months, though...Location: cannot be beatenDecor: stylish, modern, bit on the dark side, but it all works well together.Staff: Faultless. made restaurant reservation, confirmed my existing reservation, left note in my room to say they had done it. always courteous and polite. multi-lingual.Top tip: no need to get concierge to arrange a taxi - they ring for one and by the time it arrives, it already has several euros on the clock. Just walk 5 yards onto Ramblas and hail one - never took me longer than 30 seconds.

<Author>adav16
<Content>Impressive Everything about Hotel 1898, from the decor to the service and facilities were outstanding. When we arrived at 7 AM, we went up to the roof terrace, found a bed and took a nap. The downstairs pool/ jacuzzi was perfect for soothing the feet after a long day of walking. The superior room was certainly large enough for two. There was plenty of storage, robes, slippers, large tub, excellent climate control. Even the balcony, just enough to stand on, but provided a bird's eye view of the goings on in Las Ramblas. Quiet too, except I was able to hear (feel) the sound of the subway. Never did it keep me awake - perhaps a higher floor (we were on the 3rd) would help. Never used the restaurant - so many bakeries and cervesarias nearby, and the Boqueria Market. Don't buy the mango juice from the stalls in front. They charge 2 euros - the ones farther back to the side only charge 1 euro.Staff was professional, and provided everything we asked for - which was plenty! Excellent restaurant advice. Two of note: Neyras on Via Laietana 41 - easy to find - both tapas and regular menu. We ordered off the regular and were impressed.Also, El Pintor (Sant Honorat 7) in Barri Gotic off Placa Jaume. So incredibly good we went back for a second dinner before we left. Have the hotel make reservations for you! Try the salted cod with honey, pine nuts  raisins. Try the profiteroles. Seriously.Also, we found success by never taking the Turistic Bus. The bus/subway is so cheap, easy and clean. Why go all over the place when you can only really see 2 or 3 sights a day? Why wait on that horrible line? Take the 24 bus from Placa Catalunya to Park Guell. Take the subway to Sagrada Famiglia and then walk the Ruta de Modernisme following the signs in the sidewalk along the Diagonal. Take the green line Subway to the funicular up to Montjuic and see Joan Miro and the National Museum of Catalan Art. Walk through the Barri Gotic and make sure to see the Roman ruins in the basement of the Museum of le Ciutat of Barcelona. ARTICKET: if you like art, history  architecture, buy it. For 20 euros, you get entrance to 7 museums (Picasso, Joan Miro, La Pedrera, etc. - it pays for itself after three) Buy it at the tourist info center below Placa Catalunya. (Look for the I sign) Best thing: if you have the Articket, you can skip the long line at La Pedrera. Just give the ticket to the gate guard. She will get it stamped for you and you have just saved yourself a 30 minute wait!!

<Author>awtiger1
<Content>Horrible Service, Nice Building My wife and I spent two nights at the Hotel 1898 in early Oct. 2007. I am a frequent business traveler both within the US and internationally and have experience with many hotels (Four Seasons, Starwood, Ritz Carlton, etc...).Hotel 1898 is part of a chain of upscale boutique hotels in Spain. The pluses are that the hotel is in nice condition with clean rooms and good looking common spaces (including 2 pools). Our experience was ruined, however, by the incredibly unhelpful staff at Hotel 1898 who seemed to go out of their way to be outright rude to us - for instance, my wife called to ask if the conceirge could make a dinner reservation for us. Four hours later, we had heard nothing so she called again. The concierge responded by snapping that they were very busy and would call when they got around to it - by the time they did, the restaurant was fully booked. Another major problem was that the Hotel was simply mismanaged - although the check-in time was 3pm, the hotel refused to check us in at that time saying that the rooms were not clean. We were not able to check in until over two hours later and the hotel offered us no recompense for this significant inconvenience aside from one drink at the bar. I would not recommend this hotel to anyone as the service is horrendous.

<Author>DesignerDoll
<Content>Hotel 1898 - Luxury and Location We recently returned from a trip to Spain, including Barcelona, where we stayed at the Hotel 1898. We had read several reviews of this hotel; most were positive, some were not. We would absolutely recommend this beautiful hotel for adults travelling without children.The hotel's central location on the La Rambla was perfect, and after a busy and crowded day signhtseeing, the hotel's quiet and sophisticated interior was like a calming oasis for us. Although we did not eat in the hotel, we made use of the luxurious roof deck, with its pool and deep upholstered chaises (in some cases, as large as full sized beds) to read and relax. The sunsets were glorious from the roof and the roof bar served fabulous cocktails. Yes, the drinks were pricey, but certainly in line with a hotel of this quality.Our room faced a side street off La Rambla, which was great since there was a three-day festival going on during our stay, resulting in huge crowds and lots of activity. Although our room was a bit small, it had a high ceiling and luxurious appointments. We were especially impressed with the lighting and dimming control system and how well buffered we were from the noise outside. Our stay cost us $2,200.00 USD for fournights and five days in a Superior room.We had read previous reviews which were critical of the hotel's staff. We found the staff to be curteous, friendly and very helpful.Since we were arriving in Barcelona early in the morning, the hotel made arrangements to have our room ready for us earlier then the normal check-in time, secured our luggage and made a safe available for our use. With reference to the safety within and without the hotel, the staff stressed using the room safe for our valuables and being aware of the people around us in the streets while touring the city. We never had any problems or felt unsafe in Barcelona. Our favorite place to eat a light and scrumpous breakfast was Escriba, only as few blocks from the hotel. Be realistic about prices since the US Dollar is weak compared to the Euro. Expect to pay around $30.00 USD for two mini quiches, coffee, bottles of water and one (fantastic) chocolate croissant. You should make dinner reservations for popular restaurants or expect to wait until 10:00 p.m. or later to have dinner. We would suggest purchasing the one or two day tourist bus pass which provides an excellent overview of the city. You can get off and back on the bus as often as you like during a twelve hour period, allowing you to visit sites of interest for as long as you wish.Barcelona is a city not to be missed, especially if you appreciate fantastic architecture, both old and new.

<Author>Pivec
<Content>Hotel 1898 Stayed at the H1898 for 5 nights starting Sept. 12, 2007. Did take a superior room. Some comments are shown below.1) The taxi was 21 Euros from the airport. The fare was 28 Euro from the hotel to the airport--traffic was heavy in the morning. Did tip. If you request a taxi at the front desk and they call for one, the flag drops when the taxi driver receives the call. We did this once and when the taxi arrived at the hotel, the fare was already 4.5 Euros.2) The front desk was very nice and helpful. Most spoke English. We are in our middle 60's and my wife has difficulty walking because of back surgeries. We asked to see a few rooms to see which bathroom would work out the best. They showed us 3 rooms. We picked room 344--overlooked the La Rambla. Windows cut out most of the street noise.3) Room was very clean. Two twin mattresses were placed together. In the tub/shower, the top knob determined if the water came out of the spigot or the 8 shower head. The lower knob determined the water temperature. The bathroom had a hair dryer and a towel warmer rack. The room was equipped with a light dimming system--very unique. 4) The Hotel has 4 free computers for your use on the first floor.5) We did not try the breakfast. We did not think it was worth 19 Euros(26US$)/person. The room was supplied with complimentary instant coffee, teas, and a water heater. There is a Starbucks next door and a grocery store on La Rambla 1 block toward Plaza Catalunya. We picked up OJ, rolls at the bakery, and with the instant coffee,had breakfast in the room..There is a small refrigerator in the room. Afternoon tea complimentary in bar area between 5:00PM-7:00PM.6) The roof top, with pool, is very nice. Cost of a beer is 6 Euro. Spa treatments avaliable, but pricey.7) We made use of a taxi to see the various sights. Fare between 6-8 Euros. We made use of Bus 59(on the La Rambla) to get to the cable car. The cable car cost 12.5 Euro/person--round trip. Did eat at the top. Great view of the port and city.8) For dinner we ate along the La Rambla. A number of the restaurants had a daily fixed price menu--9 Euro--3 courses. One night we went to an up scale seafood restaurant along the seafront--El Cangrejo Loco. (Crazy Crab) The upstairs had an excellent view of the sea and beach. We had salad, fish(Seabass supreme and Monk), and wine. Professionally prepared and presented. Cost was 100 Euro including tip.[--]9) We did go to a Flamenco show with buffet dinner. Cost was 69 Euro/person. [--] Located at La Rambla 35--Walking distance from hotel. Would stay at the hotel again.Suggest you purchase a book by Rick Steves--Spain.Note: Be Careful. If you use a debit card, watch which one you use. I used a MasterCard and a Visa. If you use the Mastercard you are charged a 3% surcharge. At the ATM, if you withdraw 300 Euro, we were charged an extra 11US$. With the Visa, I was charged 1US$.We spent 5 nights in Barcelona and then flew to Malaga. Spent 7 nights along the Mediterranean Sea in Torremolinos at the Melia Costa del Sol.If there any questions, please do not to hesitate to Email.

<Author>sarahbeingsarah
<Content>Loved the luxury First thing about this hotel is the location, right on the Ramblas, loved it. Downsides are:The rooms are a little small and there's no view or balcony; check in is at 3 which is a bit excessive, everywhere else it's 12. The upsides way outweigh the downsides, though. The staff are very helpful and speak good English, which is a relief when you're travelling around Europe and you only speak English. The luxury level is amazing. The beds are great, really comfortable, and so are the pillows. There's a spa in the hotel which was wonderful and the rooftop bar is a great place to relax after a day's sightseeing when you want to wind down somewhere close to bed. The food at breakfast was great and there was plenty of it. The hotel is close to a metro station and easy to get to the beach, too. All up, I'd recommend this hotel.

<Author>Suparuku
<Content>Love it! For those who do not really like the indepth, nitty-gritty, I will just sumise for you right at the start. The hotel is beautiful. It's very clean, the staff speak excellent English and will answer any queries helpfully upon arrival.Right! Here's the broken down summary for those who like a thorough review.The best way I can describe it, is that it is like having complete luxury brought to your hands. You feel as though you are being treated just by being there.The maids were constantly cleaning around tables, glass (in the lift), toilets and you know that their standards are high when it comes to cleanliness.The bedroom came with en suite with toilet (and one for the men) shower, sink, shower cap, shaving foam, razor, body lotion, bubble bath, manicure set, hairdryer, robes, slippers (robe and slippers to be taken to the Spa), mini fridge, desk, box of paper and writing matrials, flat screen TV (with access to CNN and BBC News in English).The beds were very comfortable, and you are given a choice of 3 pillows to choose from, depending on which postion you sleep in. The bedding was very clean, and very contemporary. There are blankets in the cupboards incase you get a bit chilly (which we did, as the air-con came on just before we went to bed and we were unsure as to how to use the control for it). The maids did visit at about 9pm to change towels each day - which sometimes did become a little frustrating if you did want an early night they would knock until you answered the door. We did not see the need for this as we had our rooms cleaned and they changed the towels already that day, so sometimes they did not need changing.The hotel has access to the Internet and they do have a business suite however I did not visit this section of the Hotel and could not comment on the efficiency of service.Oh and in your room coffee and tea facilities are provided. Although, there are only 2 small pots of milk given and these were not replenished during our stay although other drinks sachets (i.e. coffee, tea, sugar) were. The Spa is such a fantastic thing they have on offer. We found that after a day of shopping, you would get back and feel exhaused. So to be able to use a steam room, sauna, theraputic shower and pool was like a dream come true! We found that between 7-9 the pool was empty and it felt lovely to have the peace and quiet. The pool has 2 seats, which you can sit on and activate the bubbles so that you have a kind of massage while sitting. The speed is rather fast though so you do need to hang on! The pool also has another corner dedicated to these massaging pulses of bubbles and also 2 fountains which are good for shoulder massages when standing up under them. There is also a gym facility which was also empty between 7-9pm. Towels are provided when using the Spa/Pool area but you do need to take your robe and slippers with you. There is also a shower downstairs in this area if you want to shower and change before going back to your room.The roof is also very modern and relaxing. There is a bar where all drinks are served. You can either pay there or you can charge it to your room. On one day while sitting upstairs we were given complimentary vegetable crisps to have a munch on while drinking which was an added bonus! There are sofas with cusions upstairs along with sunloungers and this was never busy so there was plenty of privacy for you, and those who prefer a topless tan (as was the case each day of our stay!).To get to the roof pool and bar, there is only 1 lift of the total 3 that get there. So if you are on the ground floor, and wanted to go to floor 7 (where it is situated) then sometimes you had to go to 6 first, then go up again to 7, which became a little tiresome. The hotel itself is situated right in the heart of La Rambia, which is a busy centre for both traffic and people. Although we could not hear the traffic or people from our rooms we could hear the music playing from the roof top bar until early hours which did actually keep me awake one night (this was without our bedroom door being open).Also our bedroom had one window, facing onto a wall of other apartment windows. We could actually see into the guest toilet opposite our apartment (not through looking, you could very easily see through) which I found a little discomfortining about the design for privacy of others.All in all an excellent stay with excellent facities and we will definately be returning

We did however get our swimsuits out of our case and enjoy the sun and the rooftop pool and bar!We had booked an upgraded room with a balcony. The room itself was large and spotlessly clean, and the balcony was huge - plenty big enough for a party!! Our room once at the back of the hotel and was very peaceful.The spa was also a great feature of the hotel giving you a great chance to unwind after a day of sightseeing and lazing on the beach. It really was a great way of calming down after the choas of the return walk home via La Rambla.The location of the hotel was great - central to all attractions, about 15-20 mins walk to eiher the beach or segrade familia.The service in the hotel is little more than functional, the reception team are very matter of fact, no smiles or friendly welcomes! This was similar throughout the hotel.I would highly recommend this hotel due to its great facilities, location and cleanliness. However dont expect fantastic over the top service and be prepared for the prices at the pool bar (8 euros for two glasses of coke!)

<Author>CriticalView
<Content>The best in Barcelona Truly great stay at Hotel 1898 - if you are headed to Barcelona there should be no other choice. Great location - easy access to all major tourist spots - neighborhoods and subways. Clean and chic interiors - great amenities - roof top pool and bar is incredibly cool with great views and stylish setting - indoor spa is unique and very chic with great mix of services - solid business center - rooms are not huge - but very well thought out decorated and clean. Two pane windows so even though we had a partial view of las rambla where on the 3rd floor and the hotel next door was under construction - noise never bothered us at all. The hotel is in the mix of Las Rambla - but it feels quiet and secluded while still being right in the mix of the city. And if you don't like crowds you should not go to Barcelona any way. Easy walking distance to the Boqeuria market - the contemporary art museum - the Gothic quarter and Picasso museum - Placa Catalan and all the other major neighborhoods - plus 2 minute walk to two major subway stations that can take you anywhere you else you might want to go. I travel all the time stay at 5 star (Four Seasons etc) - this is just as good as any 5 start hotel. When we get back to Barcelona - we will stay here without a doubt - its not cheap - but its well worth the money - cant think of a single thing I would change. The perfect place to say for a visit to this great city.

<Author>contented_wanderers
<Content>Beautiful, stylish hotel Let me make this clear from the start, Hotel 1898 is not cheap. However, it is gorgeous. It is very stylish and chic without being all trendy and aloof! The reception staff were very helpful every time we spoke with them. They provided lots of eating recommendations and had three or four books worth of menus and pictures to help choose. The only issue was with the staff at the roof top bar who didn't seem very keen to come over and get you more drinks (although we could have gone up and got them ourselves if we weren't lounging on the big sofas in the sun!).We had a deluxe room which had it's own balcony. That was a definite advantage and we ate breakfast there each morning (although we did buy our own from the supermarket a few doors down rather than pay the 19 euros each the hotel wanted). The bathroom was a reasonable size with a lovely deep bath, and a huge shower head. Also the room was very clean and was serviced well each day.The food in the restaurant was superb and the service extremely friendly. The complimentary appetizer was delicious, and the other courses were just as good. It was the nicest restaurant we ate at although we were a bit unorganised at booking other restaurants - which is advisable if you want to go to a top level restaurant, we missed out on one promising venue because they were jam packed all evening. After reading other people's comments about the noise level from La Rambla we were a bit worried about being able to sleep. But there was no noise issue with our sound proofed room (which of course won't work if you open the window - there's no need as the room was very well air conditioned!). We slept soundly each night in the huge bed which you can customise with the pillow menu!

<Author>RobFindlater
<Content>Excellent hotel, consistent high standards There is very little to add as its all been said before by other reviewers. However its hopefully useful to mention that everything positive that has been written was still in evidence when my wife and I stayed there for 2 nights earlier this week.I booked to stay in a Priviledge Room which is larger than the standard rooms and situated on the corners of the hotel overlooking Las Ramblas. Interestingly I found that these rooms were only on offer by booking direct with the hotel.Our room was comfortable, very modern and spotlessly clean and had all the services we have come to expect from travelling.A nice touch was also the free computers, Internet access and printers on the 1st floor in the Library area as this allowed us to check-in online and print our boarding passes for the journey back to the UK which saved some hassle at the airport.We went to the hotel restaurant for one night and while the menu sounded excellent and the prices were comparable with a high quality establishment we didn't end up eating there as it was rather quiet that night so atmosphere was lacking.The roof terrace pool and bar is a nice touch, as is the underground swimming pool complex where again all the basic facilities are free of charge.Location is perfect on Las Ramblas and our taxi drivers had no issue finding the place.To summarise an absolutely fantastic place that deserves its top position on Tripadvisor and I'd be very happy to stay there again and would thoroughly recommend it.

<Author>Actomon
<Content>Excellent Hotel - Tranquility in the madness of Ramblas We have just returned from 3 nights in the 1898 celebrating my 40th Birthday. Being No1 on trip advisor was the reason we booked this hotel. We read the very few negatives on here and this is what i think. You will always get people who are never satisfied with anything, you know the type. they are at the reception desks screaming at the staff about the slightest issue, no wonder then they get nothing sorted because lets face it, no place or event in the world is perfect and i suppose the true test of a hotel is how they react when things go slightly wrong because hey this is the reality of every day life. So firstly we got to our room, great room but right outside the elevator, based on previous comments i didnt want to settle in the room and find i could hear the elevators through the night (im a light sleeper) so we went down to reception straight away and explained.(by the way they have removed the lift bell on those floors now anyway) we got a better room issued immediately ! Result ! But you know what, if you speak politely without attitude and explain the issue, 99 times out 100, you get it sorted, and thats the point about the negatives reviews here. Next we ordered some bollinger off the menu at 80 euro's, good price i thought, when we got the bill it had 130 euro's on it, on checking the menu i had been given an old menu, no problem sir the correct price is actually 130 euro which i have to charge you but what i will give you is free drinks for the rest of the night !!!(we drunk easily more than twice the diff)- result No 2. Next morning we ordered 2 types of breakfast, they only brought one, on ringing the kitchen they apologised and the other was with us within 3 mins - result no 3. The reception were very helpful with ordering taxis( you cant be charged double going to the airport because they are all on meters NB previous review) and booking restaurants, in fact they got us into a restaurant that was full because they regularly send customers there. We didnt really do any site seeing, it was relax in the sun, wine and dine break and the hotel is perfect for that. The Ramblas outside the hotel is madness in august, it is so busy, so when you step back into the hotel it is like an Oasis of calm and tranquility, and for the previous comment about the bar been quite - what do you want when you have been in crowds of people all day ! certainly not queueing with hoards of noisy people at the bar. If your looking for the better bars and restaurants then turn left has you come out the hotel onto the Ramblas and walk couple of 100 yards up, this way you get away from all the tourists coming off the boats and getting trapped in the Ramblas restaurants which are poor food/high prices. 2 places were excellent, a traditional tapas bar called Alfonso for lunch and theTralaguz restaurant for a big night meal.

<Author>LMtraveler
<Content>Great Hotel Hotel 1898 is a very beautiful hotel in the heart of the market section of Las Ramblas. Everything you could possibly need is within two blocks of the hotel. The rooms are all high tech, spotless, and beautifully designed. They are small by American standards, but not an inch of space is wasted. We stayed in two superior, double rooms. The beds were big and comfortable and you have your choice of pillows. The bathrooms are large and gorgeous - all marble and chrome, with towel warmers and showers with full bathtubs. Everything is state-of-the art, which meant that sometimes we had to call the front desk to figure out how to get things to work. The common areas are open, beautiful and inviting. Staff is professional and friendly and you can always find someone who speaks English. There is a small swimming pool on top of the hotel, with a bar and a deck from which you can view all of Barcelona. The hotel is on a part of Las Ramblas that is packed with tourists, but it is fun to walk down the street and see all of the street artists and visit the vendors. The surrounding streets are lined with stores, good restaurants and cafes. We only spent one night in Barcelona en route to somewhere else, but Hotel 1898 was one of the highlights of our trips.  
<Date>Aug 5, 2007

<Author>Francois_Verhaart
<Content>Really enjoyed Hotel 1898 My wife and I stayed at Hotel 1898 for 2 nights at the end of July for a long weekend. The hotel, located in a beautifully restored old building in a very central location, looks new and well-kept. The (standard) room, while not very big, had a clean and fresh feel to it. The bathroom was nice with a great shower and good water pressure. The reception staff was very friendly and helpful and spoke English very well. On our last day we were able to extend our room stay until 6pm for about 40% of what we paid for a full night. Maybe not cheap, but it allowed us to fully enjoy the day and freshen up before heading back to the airport. We particularly enjoyed the rooftop pool and lounge area. It was very warm when we were in Barcelona and after some sightseeing in the city, it was a great place to relax for a few hours and have some drinks. That brings me to the only negative thing of this hotel. The prices for drinks on the rooftop were excessive; we paid almost 15 euros per drink for a rum  cola and a mojito. We also used the indoor pool downstairs, which is beautiful. We will definitely come back here for our next trip to Barcelona.

<Author>timotao
<Content>Wonderful Hotel in Barcelona My wife and I were in Spain this July for a two week visit, starting and ending in Barcelona, with stops at Valencia, Denia and Granada in between. The Hotel we had first booked in Barcelona, the Hotel Jazz, also a part of the Nunez/Navarro chain, informed us they were full (due to a cancelled airline flight) when we arrived late on a Monday evening. At first our hearts sank, but they then informed us that they were transferring our reservation, at the same rates, to another hotel in the NN chain in Barcelona, the H1898. What seemed at first might be a disaster turned out to be great good luck: the H1898 hotel is a beautiful property, staffed by professional and considerate hoteliers in the old sense. The building itself is an historic site that has been superbly renovated with furnishings and decor and fitments of high quality. It is warm, welcoming, comfortable everywhere: the rooms, the lobby, the restaurant, the bars.The location couldn't be better: on the Rambla, at the edge of El Raval, and close to everything we wanted to see: the Bari Gotic with the old Cathedral, the Museu Picasso, and its side streets; the El Raval itself with MACBA and CCCB; the Paseo de Graciawith the Fundacio Antoni Tapies and La Perdrera; Parc Montjuic with the Fundacio Joan Miro; and the Sagrada Familia a short subway ride (3 stops) away.The hotel staff were terrific: most had English skills superior to our Spanish skills, and communication was pleasant and easy.At the front desk, at the door, in the bars and the restaurant, all the staff were polite, extremely considerate, and willling to go out of their way to help. Even when busy they were patient and understanding.The H1898 boasts some extras you might not find at other hotels: first, a rooftop terrasse with a pool and a bar, a perfect place to have a late afternoon swim and an evening cava plus a terrific view of the Barcelona skyline and rooftops, down to the Old Port and the harbour; second, a pool/sauna/spa complex in a large stone grotto downstairs: magical and relaxing.We liked H1898 so much after our first two nights there at the start of our trip that we cancelled our reservations at the hotel we had booked for our last week in Barcelona and booked into H1898, and had five wonderful days in a charming, lively,dynamic city made better by having H1898 as our base.

<Author>FrequentTraveller69
<Content>Central, fantasic hotel. This hotel very well placed being on La Rambla. Close to the main square and shopping ares and close to the beautiful harbour area. The hotel is very chic with good sized airy, well decorated rooms with large plasma TVs. The bathroom was also spacious (as far as hotel bathrooms go) with marble units and, very important... a proper glass shower screen rather than a shower curtain. The roof terrace is very nice and kept clean although the small pool is very cold. The pool in the basement is great but a little dark. <Author>Go Travel Europe
<Content>Great Hotel AND Great Service We loved the hotel and felt they also provided great service. <Author>Nicoleanarose
<Content>Honeymooners at Hotel 1898 We went to Hotel 1898 for our honeymoon from June 21-30th (we are 26  29). First off, I would highly recommend this hotel, but there are some things that need some improvement. I understand that my new husband and I are used to five star accomodations in Latin America and the States so the may scew our view a bit. Well, here is a summary of our impression of the hotel.Arrival: We flew Miami to Barcelona (via Madrid) by Iberia. It was a travel disaster. Iberia is the absoluate WORST airline we have ever traveled on. It was more like being on a bus, but I won't bore you with the details. Let me just say they are poorly informed (we both native Spanish speakers, so it wasn't a communication problem), rude and the food was inedible. We are not tall people (5'8, 5'11) and we were smashed into our seats. Anyhow, we made it to the beautiful hotel at around 1 p.m. We figured are room would not be ready and we were right. We went and grabbed a quick lunch and waited in the lobby. The concierge sent us up to the roof for a complimentary glass of Champagne at 2:30 and told is it would be a bit longer (I think he wanted us out of the lobby, we looked a bit shabby). At 3 p.m. we checked and were escorted to our room.Room: We had room 535, it had a HUGE terrace which made the somewhat small room seem much larger! The bathroom was nicer and larger than expected. It had an oversized tub and great bathing products. We really took advantage of our terrace. We bought cheese, wine, and ham at the loca Carrefour Express and listened to our Ipod on the balcony many nights before going out. The room was decorated beautifully, with deep reds and black and white. The bed and pillows were delicious! We were very pleased.Service: I would give them a C (I am a teacher). This is where they need some work, they do not bend over backwards. My husband is Colombian and we both speak Spanish. We found the people in the hotel to be cold and uninviting. The lobby was dead, which we really didn't mind because there are much cooler places in BRC, but they need friendlier service, especially when we were paying top dollar for 9 nights in a top room at the hotel!Amenities: We took advantage of both pools. We are from Miami, so we found the pool on the roof to be FREEZING, but it was a great way to cure a hangover and tired feet! The pool in the Spa was always deserted and was very romantic. We used the steam and sauna, but didn't use any spa services as they were booked when we wanted them. I think they should keep the pool in the Spa open later. It closes at 9 p.m., which seems really early for a city that doesn't eat dinner until 10:30 pm.Food: We ate lunch there on our first day. It was okay. I had a pretty yummy salad and my husband had some rice dish. We felt it was overpriced, but the view is beautiful from the roof and the beds were nice to sit on. We had breakfast one day before a long day of touring and although a bit pricey we thought it was great. We ordered room service once (a fruit salad and club sandwich) it arrived promptly and was quite good. We never ate dinner there because there are SOOO many good restaurants in Barcelona.Summing it up, the hotel is VERY centrally located and is an oasis in the noisy and sometimes frustrating Las Ramblas. It is the most gorgeous structure on the block and it a very relaxing place to hang you hat after a long day of touring or partying. In the end, we were VERY happy with our stay. We just think they need a bit more work on their manners and need to spice it up a bit (a little soft music by the pool maybe?). We were on our honeymoon, so really we were going to be happy no matter what. If you have any questions feel free to contact me.Here are some suggestions for Barcelona:1) Do the Tourbus(it is a great way to see the city and its main sights)2) Walk down to the beach, eat lunch, and lay out on a towel and watch people in their swimsuits (or lack there of). 3) Eat at Tragaluz. We ate next to Woody Allen the night we were there, but the food was so good I didn't notice until on our way out!4) Buy the Top 10 Guide to Barcelona (it has great suggestions and is well organized and it fits in your handbag)5) If you like the 'scene go to CDLD and eat some sushi and then buy a bed and party until 6 a.m.6) Eat tapas at Taller de Tapas, they are the BEST tapas in the city in a lively environment.7) See Goudi, even if it is not your thing.Have Fun!

<Author>ffnoddy
<Content>Beautiful Hotel with indifferent staff ! Stayed at the 1898 on the basis of previous reviews and arrived with Great expectations ..... maybe I should've taken the novel, because the expectations were only partly realised !The hotel is in a fantastic location right on La Rambla  within walking distance of loads of Barcelona's attractions. The 1898 is beatifully presented with all of the facilities you may need for a short stay. The room was as we requested, spacious, well equipped and very clean, although the views were pretty dissappointing.The rooftop pool is a must after a day wandering around Barcelona trying to figure out how Gaudi persuaded builders to start his wonderful projects  you'll get the views you'll wish you had from your room here. The restaurant is good  the wine massage in the underground spa is a must.We only ordered room service on our last morning, which was very nice, although a little late. But the glass of Cava with breakfast more than made up for it !We did have a few issues with the service at the hotel though.The lock on our door was faulty, which resulted in the room being left open by the maid a couple of times .... fortunately nothing went amiss.When we reported the problem, we were surprised to find that the staff felt we were ruining their day by interupting more important things they had to do! Not the service I'd expect from a 4 star.Concierge facilities were pretty much non-existent, so take a guide book ! ..... when we tried to get the hotel to order a taxi upon our departure, we felt it would've been easier to wander the streets of Barcelona for a couple hours in the blazing heat, dressed in a ski suit, holding aloft a sign in spanish saying 'I hate taxi drivers' !!However ......... Don't be put off staying here. The hotel is great despite the majority of the staff  we did still have a great time ...... probably due to the sangria from the bars on La Rambla !If the staff smiled every now and then and did as you asked this would be a fantastic hotel.

<Author>JonathanB777
<Content>The 1898 - A Fair Assessment... I rely on tripadvisor quite heavily on selecting a hotel to stay in but it is always important to read between the lines of the various comments. The reviews of the 1898 range from the sublime to the underwhelmed and in fairness both are fair descriptions but also true of any other ranked hotel in Barcelona. This is an extremely comfortable hotel which is fantastically well appointed. If staying in summer the ability to get away from it all and sunbathe by a roof-top pool may for many make it worthwhile in itself. There is also a well equipped gymn and OK Spa. We never had breakfast in the hotel (20 euros ahead!) but worth missing for all the excellent alternatives on the doorstep. The rooms are very comfortable and fully equipped (although the plasmas volume is set to such a low maximum volume that you can't hear them even in your own room). The gentleman who said it was a bit soulless in the bar and reception areas is correct and some of the staff (especially the bar man) could definately have done with a happy fix. All that said this is probably still a good choice for a few days stay in a simply breathtaking city. If you book a room make SURE you get a small balcony at least (we asked to be moved) and I imagine not looking over La Ramblas itself. If you are looking for the hotel to Make your Stay then this may disappoint (as probaly will most others). If you are looking for a fine place to explore and enjoy then it has much to recommend it.P.S I am being very nice by not mentioning that they took 25 minutes to bring our bags from our room when our taxi meter was running (i'm not proud I would rather have brought them down ourselves!)

<Author>travelmom333
<Content>A hidden treasure I wavered between choosing a hotel based upon a local business owner's recommendation and my own search and Trip Advisor. I couldn't have been more pleased with my own search. Following a horrific beginning to my trip (business trip where my luggage was lost and my credit cards, passport and money stolen) where I stayed at a terrible HUSA hotel, I felt as if I had died and gone to heaven when I finally arrived at Hotel 1898. The hotel is beautiful, elegant, clean, professional and exceptionally located without having to be in the middle of the Las Ramblas noise and craziness. I stayed in one of the quiet rooms overlooking the courtyard and it was perfect. My daugher likened this hotel to an elegant cruise ship with the dark wood trim, plush carpets and brass hardware along the hallway.The room was spacious by European standards and was well equiped including very nice toiletries, bathrobes and slippers and tea service. The beds were comfortable although not plush. Internet connection was brisk and there was a good sampling of english language TV stations. The hotel is in very close proximity to the metro and around the corner from Las Ramblas although very quiet and secluded. The lobby has a tea time and cocktail hour but I never saw much action there. There is a roof top deck but my daughter and I were out exploring until late so never had a chance to use it. We had the American Breakfast served to our room. Service was prompt and for those longing for a good American Breakfast, this was it! It was so plentiful, we only needed one tray for the 2 of us.If you are going to Barcelona, search no more. Hotel 1898 is an experience everyone should have. Enjoy!

<Author>ASC
<Content>Loved it! We had a wonderful long weekend away - just the two of us for a birthday celebration - and would happily recommend this hotel.We booked this hotel on the strength of the Trip Advisor reviews and so were aware that the room we had chosen was small, however it was perfectly formed with everything we could have needed. Yes, the hairdrier was a little tricky, so I would advise taking your own if you have very long hair or would have difficulty in holding down the rocker switch continually. On the plus side the heated bathroom mirrors never got misted up so perfect for make-up and so on.Just a note to anybody wishing to book a room with a terrace, we were located on the 6th floor and the rooms with terraces were on the 5th floor directly below us so we had a clear view onto what may be considered a private area. We were not disturbed by any street noise because again, we knew from previous reviews that it's a good idea to request a quiet room. We were next to the lifts, but were not particularly bothered by them - but then we did go to bed quite late! We did not eat breakfast in the hotel until the last day, partly because of the price, partly because it is so lovely to sit out in the morning sunshine at one of the many cafes serving breakfast. We did take the hotel breakfast before leaving for the airport - it was lovely but expensive all the same.My final point is that the roof terrace is stunning with amazing views over the city. This brings me to our one moan and that is there is a roped off area to the right of the bar with beautiful day beds in the evening sun and well sheltered from the wind. We told we could only use this area if we were drinking cocktails from a rather pricey list (14 euros for a mojito). We did go ahead (too beautiful not too), but felt that if you are paying to stay in the hotel then really all guests should be treated equally. By the way, you cannot sunbathe in this section and so cover up and wear shoes - there is no sign to indicate this but the bar staff won't let you in otherwiseTo sum up, we wouldn't hesitate to stay there again!

<Author>CIARB
<Content>Not as good as it has been cracked up to be We were expecting to be staying in a truly remarkable hotel given the recent reviews (making it the No.1 hotel in Barcelona) and the price. Whilst it is an excellent hotel in so many ways it is also a soulless sort of place - the lounges, bars and restaurants were practically empty for the whole duration of our stay. Whilst we don't like crowded hotels, this one was more like a morgue than a hotel. Management needs to have a rethink, because the hotel has the makings of a great hotel - but it will never be that so long as they serve mediocre food and overpriced drinks, and have second rate staff performance. By way of example, the male receptionist who greeted us was the most miserable soul I have had the misfortune to meet for quite a while. We are used to staying in 5* hotels worldwide and the 1898 unfortunately misses the mark by quite a wide margin, both on price and service; I find it hard to believe that, according to Tripadvisor reviewers, it is Barcelona's finest - I guess it deserves a ranking of about #10 at best - but there again I haven't sampled the others yet.

<Author>AvidHolidaymaker
<Content>Fab choice for Barcelona! Booked Hotel 1898 based on previous TA reviews and was not disappointed! It's all been said before - what more can I add?! If you arrive at the airport, just take the airport bus from immediately outside the Terminal door (3.90 Euros per person) as it takes you right into Plaza Catalunya and it's just a short walk round to La Rambla and a couple of blocks down on the right you'll find the hotel.The Hotel is actually an old building (which used to house the Philipine Tobacco company) but was beautifully restored just 2 years ago. We paid 199 Euros per night for a classic room (supposedly their most basic but it was perfect). Our room faced onto an inner courtyard and was very peaceful. To re-iterate previous reviews, all the positive points of the Hotel: location, interior design, spacious public areas, lovely rooftop terrace, beautiful rooms and bathrooms, immaculately clean. Two (very tiny) negative points - (but in no way should it stop you from booking!): the hairdryer was a bit cumbersome and awkward to use, and, while the rooftop terrace is a huge asset in a city centre hotel, the number of loungers is a bit limited. However, after a day's walking  sightseeing, this is a lovely relaxed area with cushioned benches to flop with one of their marvellous glasses of sangria! The breakfast was 19 Euros each - a bit pricey but the quality was excellent (cereals, freshest of fruit, pastries, breads, smoked salmon, cheeses, meats, omelettes made to order etc.) We also used the Royal Hotel just up the road - good value at 9 Euros but not quite the same quality. There is also a Starbucks attached to the hotel if you just fancy a coffee and a muffin one morning. Further down La Rambla, La Boqueria food market is wonderful for a walk round - and you could just pick up fresh fruit, pastries etc there!4 restaurants tested and definitely able to recommend, none too far from Hotel 1898:1. Can Culleretes, C/Quintana 5 (oldest restaurant in Barcelona and cheap too).2. Taller de Tapas, C/Argenteria 51 ( very busy but good tapas).3. Els Quatre Gats, C/Montsio3 (full of character and live music too).4. Les Quince Nits, Plaza Reial (popular with the locals too).Things to do (some obvious!): open top bus tour (23 Euros for 2 days with Bus Turistic), walk down La Rambla watching all the street entertainment, take the lift to the top of the Columbus monument, visit some of Gaudi's buildings (Casa Batllo, La Pedrera, Sagrada Familia), visit the Museu D'Historia for a great insight into Roman Barcelona, visit Poble Espanyol to see the different Spanish styles of building and see the different crafts, tour round FC Barcelona stadium. I actually think Barcelona would be a great place to take children too - apart from the places already mentioned, there's the beach, zoo, aquarium etc!I will definitely go back, and will definitely book Hotel 1898 again! Enjoy!  
<Date>Jun 25, 2007

<Author>meovcorse
<Content>disappointing. 5* building run as 2-3* hotel Stayed here at the begining of June having chosen it after reading the reviews on this site but were very disappointed. On the positive side, the location is unbeatable, the decor beautiful and the hotel very clean. But.....We arrived well after check in time but our room was not ready and had to wait nearly half an hour for it. We were given a chit to take to the bar for a complementary drink whilst we waited. We went to the bar which was unattended, there was no bell or any way of attracting attention. We could here the staff in the room behind the bar so, after 7 or 8 minutes, we politely called out to them. We were very surprised (and shocked) when a male voice shouted back wait a minute. A couple of minutes later a female opened the door, poked her head out, and again said wait a minute. It was a further 2-3 minutes before we eventually were served.We booked a de-luxe room which was small, as we expected having read the reviews here, however, it was the terrace that really disappointed us. We selected the de-luxe room specifically for the terrace which was not only much smaller than expected ( the ones either side of ours were much bigger) but also instead of the stone balustrading shown in the pictures, we had a solid wall facing us which not only allowed us no view, but also made it dark and quite dingy. There was no seperate shower cubicle as some other rooms seem to have. Our room was by the elevator and there was the constant noise of the elevator pinging and of other guest laughing and joking throughout the night (fault of the room not the guests).Having missed eating one evening we discovered that room service finished at 11pm. There was absolutely no food available in the hotel after this hour. I have never before come across a hotel that couldn't russle up at least a basic sandwich, even if nothing else. Breakfast was the worst part of the experience. It was very poor but pricey (19 euros). Having sat ourselves down and having waited several minutes, we had to call the attention of one of the waiters, who had totally ignored us up to that point, to ask for tea and coffee. When it eventually came, nearly 10 minutes later, the coffee was fine but tea was a cup of hot water and a point at the teabags on the table. No milk and when requested, hot milk was brought. I should mention that the room was not even half full so there was no excuse of being busy or them being rushed off their feet.The cooked food was not only not freshly cooked, but the pre-cooked food was placed on a normal, unheated counter therefore it was barely warm and very unappetising. This is truely the worst breakfast, food and service, that I have received anywhere, including in 3rd world countries and travelodges! There were several other niggles that I won't mention now.I wondered afterwards about the great reviews that have been given here and realised that had we:1. arrived an hour later - we would not have known that our room wasn't ready and would not have gone to the bar and experienced the problems there.2. been allocated a different room, there are clearly better de-luxe rooms - we would not have been disappointed with the terrace.3. been allocated a room away from the elevator - we would not have been woken up several times a night or been aware that some guest were experiencing that.4. not missed our evening meal - we would not have wanted food at midnight therefore we would not have known that it was not available.5. not had breakfast in the hotel - we would not have known how bad it was.Had none of the above things occurred we would have gone away having feeling that we had stayed in a well located, clean, beautiful looking hotel. We would have been unaware of the shortcomings of it, and, in ignorance, given it an undeserved very good, review.Maybe we were just unlucky with our room allocation, but unless you have been there before and specifically request to have or ask not to be given a particular room, you can't know whether you have been allocated a good or a poor room. A good hotel should offer a consistently good experience, which ever room you are in or whatever time/period you stay there in. Hotel 1898 does not offer this consistency. We may have been unlucky BUT SO MIGHT YOU BE!!!The building has the makings of a 5* hotel but unfortunately it is run like a 2-3* one.

<Author>camdencalling
<Content>No wonder it's the tops! Thanks reviewers! Definitely a great choice! Visiting Barca for a friend's wedding in the Gothic quarter, this hotel was the obvious choice. I've stayed in Barca several times before in the Rambla area but this hotel is streets ahead of the others. A superb conversion of an old building, well and truly sound-proofed and with fabulous facilities for a hotel in this position, it is hard to find fault with it. Possibly some may find the rooms a bit on the small side and rather dark. But dark is the theme of the hotel throughout and is extremely smart. Our room looked inwards onto a courtyard and directly into several other hotel rooms but that wasn't a problem - better that than having street traffic. Rather silly controls for the lights (letting the designers lose is a dangerous thing sometimes!) meant that you had to have both bedside lights on or off at the same time. But on the plus side, the rooftop bar area with a small pool and masses of lounging space has superb views all over Barcelona, and downstairs in the basement, the small pool has jet corners for getting out the aches after too much shopping in La Rambla. Breakfast is expensive at 鈧?9 but with so many fabulous cafes and the fabulous, famous food market next door, who needs it! Altogether a superb city hotel.

<Author>JoesBrigade
<Content>One of the best ever We stayed 3 nights and picked this based on Tripadvisor reviews. We were not disappointed as, whilst it isn't the cheapest hotel, the facilities and the staff are extremely good. The rooftop pool and comfy seats were a really oasis after a busy day and the views were fantastic. The rooms, and in particular the bathrooms, were of the highest standard but the best of all was down in the basement. The pool may have been small but it was never too busy and, on top of excellent sauna and steam room, the pool had 2 water jets, the jacuzzi jets and jets in metal loungers in the pool to massage yourself with.You cannot fault the quality of the hotel decor and the location is in the middle of Las Ramblas and so easy to go in either direction. Drinks were a bit expensive and whilst breakfast at 19 euros may be expensive for some, there was a Continental option at 9 euros.One of the best and easiest hotels we've ever stayed in.

<Author>PaulaJ0
<Content>Fantastic !!! What a fantastic hotel !!! I took my fiance for a surprise 40th birthday present and what a brilliant time we had. The hotel is grand without being too pretentious. I booked directly with the hotel (which is cheaper than through an agency) and explained that this was a special occasion and could they allocate an extra special room. When we checked in I mentioned this and although our booking was for a classic room, we were placed in a fabulous room with its own terracing (room 202). The room itself was maybe not the biggest but the attention to detail cannot be faulted. The choice of lighting, the digital radio, the tea/coffee facilities (but take some teabags along if you need your fix first thing in the morning!), the bathroom is stunning and not to mention the spa, pool and steam rooms. What an absolute pleasure it was. Las Ramblas is an experience, the city bus tour a waste of money as its much nicer to walk to attractions. We will certainly be going back to Barcelona and will stay at Hotel 1898 again. Have fun !!!

<Author>Coffeeman1960
<Content>Perfect for a short break We have just returned from a 3-night break in early May. The H1898 is a well-presented modern boutique-style hotel in an absolutely fabulous central location on Las Ramblas. Despite the busy location the hotel was an oasis of calm and our room (which faced into a central courtyard/atrium) was quiet whatever the hour.We found service to be pleasant and prompt; the wonderful breakfast extensive and reasonable value at 19 Euro; the public lounge areas comfortable and impressive; the rooftop lounge/pool area fantastic (though with so much to see we didn't have much time to use it); and the basement pool/spa well presented (even if the pool was a little on the cool side).If we were being critical we might say that the hotel is a little dark, mainly due to the style and finishes (our room saw little daylight) and the room and bathroom could have been larger.Overall I would heartlily recommend this hotel. Given the wide choice available in a city like Barcelona we chose it for it's high tripadvisor rating. If you do the same we don't think you will be disappointed.

<Author>Ronaldobiscottini
<Content>Loved it, Loved it, Loved it I agonised for quite some time about which hotel to book for our 3-night stay in April (back yesterday - depressed!).Once I had seen 1898, I kept coming back to it and booked it once I had gotten my head around paying so much for the hotel (拢156 per night incl breakfast). Well, my wife and I were not disappointed - FANTASTIC. Here is the good stuff:The decor in the hotel is exquisite, so tastefully done that you could while away many hours just chilling in the lounge or bar. Our room was small but perfectly formed, really classy decor again, great bed, a choice of pillows(!), plasma tv, great bathroom etc etc. Everything you could possibly want.What made the hotel for us was actually what was above the hotel, i.e. the rooftop deck and pool - awesome. I'm afraid some of the Barcelona attractions took a back seat each day as we chilled with our sangrias by the pool, with the mild din of la rambla in the background. Yes, the drinks were expensive, but worth it in our opinion. The basement spa area was also really nice, although we only used it once because the weather was so nice! The location is also great, right on the rambla for convenience, but once inside, you would never know it.Not so good:Some people mentioned noise in their reviews which concerned me, as I am a light sleeper. I was woken two of the three nights, but that was by people coming back to their rooms. I never heard the maid service etc at all and this wouldn't stop me staying here again. Better sleepers probably woudln't have heard anything.I didn't find the staff to match up to the overall 5 stars (although still 4 stars). For example, we sent an email in advance requesting a quiet room and never got a response, and generally the level of servive could I think be a bit better.SummaryOverall, I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel, especially if you want to stay somewhere where you can happily spend some time relaxing, rather than charging around Barca. I would thoroughly recommend staying somewhere (if not 1898) that has a rooftop pool.Final point - due to my estensive research beforehand (AKA procrastination), I recognised quite a few hotel names as we explored Barca. Montecarlo is right opposite 1898 and looked nice from the outside - again, great location. Passed Casa Camper on last day, near the University, looked nice. Torre de Catalunya is right next to Sants station and too far out of the action in my opinion.

<Author>Al_and_J
<Content>Good Hotel, but Not Exceptional Value We stayed for four days at this hotel last week (the week after Easter). I would say the hotel is perfectly adequate for a 4 star hotel, with reasonably-sized rooms and adequate service, but perhaps not quite the top notch status as some other reviews might suggest. Although we have no real complaints about the hotel (it justifies its 4-stars), we are not convinced of the premium it seems to command. (It would, for example, have been cheaper for us to stay at the Claris, the Sofia Gran or the Hilton Diagonal Del Mar - all 5 star hotels).What you're paying for, I guess, is its very central location at the heart of town, and close to attractions/amenities such as the ramblas, the gothic quarter and near to transport links.It also has a panoramic roof terrace, with good seating and an outdoor pool (which was surprisingly warm at this time of year), as well as a small (and stone cold) indoor pool and spa. However, there is only one restaurant, and one bar (based round the lobby) and one cafe (not counting the resident Starbucks). The restaurant is competitively priced (at least in hotel terms), but was surprisingly devoid of guest, as it is very easy to eat out (which we did on a couple of nights). The breakfast buffet has a diverse range, and is good value if included in your booking.Overall, this is a competent and well-located hotel, particularly if you can get a competitive rate (which was hard for us, even three months out). However, for the price of 230 euros/拢160, it's not quite in the same league as (for example) the Plaza in New York, Claridges in London, or the Shangri La's in Asia. (It's more akin to the Malmaison boutique chain in the UK - but perhaps costing slightly more, with fewer extra touches.)Having said this, though, our stay was pleasant and comfortable, and our only complaint (if that's the right word), is that they sting you 16 euros to advertise one of their flaky umbrellas when it rains. (Guests staying in the hotel opposite were treated to complimentary Meridien golf umbrellas.) As for Barcelona, if this is rated as one of the best hotels, then all the other 4 (and 5) star hotels in the city must be considerably wanting. We observed that, although we speak three different languages, it definitely helps to speak Spanish (and specifically the local Catalonian dialect), else you tend to be treated as a second-class citizen with all but the most service-conscious locals (who are few and far between, from our experience). Petty theft in the area also seems surprisingly common - we even met a well-travelled couple who got their handbag/purse stolen by thieves who threw pidgeon poo at them (and used it as a distraction for robbing them).  
<Date>Apr 18, 2007

<Content>An Easter treat! We recently stayed for 3 nights at this hotel over Easter having been upgraded from its sister hotel Jazz, which we orignally booked, due to a computer booking problem. Also the hotel smelled lovely throughout! We will book this hotel again when we return to Barcelona.

<Content>Excellent Hotel We visited over the first weekend of April 2007 having seen the good reviews written here, and weren't disappointed. Everything about the hotel was excellent. <Author>LGAtlanta
<Content>Service hiccups and very noisy! I stayed at the Hotel 1898 March 26-31 and was disappointed. In fact, I'm writing this at 2am the night before a long trans-Atlantic flight back to the States because I can't sleep! It sounds like there's a club in my room ... it's so loud that I can sing along with the music when my head isn't about to explode from the club beat. Apparently, there's a nearby club that literally rocks the house on the weekends. BTW, they're currently playing Flashdance so the club has questionable music taste.The hotel itself is reasonably nice but the service doesn't match the decor. Other reviewers have noted the location but, believe me, there are lots of hotels in the same location to choose from - it doesn't have to be this one.My primary purpose of being in Barcelona was business and, as such, my key complaints are those of a business traveler looking for service and efficiency ... definitely not what I found:(1) I wasn't offered a map of the city when I checked in(2) I had problems with temperature control in my room. I spent a couple of warm days in the room before calling the front desk to look at the AC, which they said was turned off .... why, they couldn't say. It certainly wasn't obvious the AC was turned off because it's tucked into a side of the closet that requires a sleuthing operation to find.(3) The hair dryer is one of the worst I've ever seen ... It feels like no exagerration to say it weighs a ton and you have to hold down the button continually to keep the dryer on. I had dents in my thumbs after I finished drying my hair.(4) In general, I had a lot of problems with noise .... there was a lot of hammering away in different parts of the hotel during the day and housekeeping was always really loud. I had to call the front desk twice about noise just so I could sleep away some jet lag for 1 hour in the late afternoon.(5) It's impossible to get a taxi at the hotel. This is a real issuefor people staying at the hotel for business reasons. I was late toa conference 2 days in a row because it took so long to get a taxi. The hotel apparently has no special relationships with taxi companies.(6) I had to call the front desk to get information on accessing theInternet. I don't understand why this wouldn't be explained atcheck-in or on a sheet/placard in the room. I spent 5-10 minutes searching for this information in the room before I finally gave up and called the front desk.(7) The hotel gym is missing one of the set of two weights that I use in my workouts. The weight was missing all week so it didn't seem like anyone was in a hurry to replace it. This may seem like a minor issue, but it added up to a general inattention to the detail that creates a good hotel experience.

<Author>Rebecca004
<Content>Fantastic - a great hotel in a brilliant location What a great hotel. We booked a standard room for a long weekend as a bit of a treat, and it was well worth the money. We called ahead and asked to be on a high floor and at the front (after reading comments about the noise from the club below), and were given a fantastic room with a view over the Ramblas. The room and bathroom were big, the bed huge, and the decor throughout was stylish without being desperately trendy. The location could not have been better; we felt pleased to be back there whenever we returned. We were on the third floor - you could hear the club below, but only vaguely. <Author>minijaffacake74
<Content>Loved, Loved Loved it! Stayed at this hotel 17 to 20 March and loved every minute of it. Definately the nicest hotel we have ever stayed at. The lobby/reception/bar area is gorgeous. The roof top deck was a fantastic chill out area, but was a bit too windy when we were there to try out the roof top pool. We did spend a couple of hours in the basement spa pool and had it all to ourselves which was wonderful. We had booked a classic room which is listed as having an inner atrium courtyard view, however, when we shown to our room 606, on the 6th floor, we actually had an outside view, overlooking some of the private terraces of the rooms below. It wasn't a bad view by any means and as we were expecting an inside room then to have an outside view and be able to see the sun was a bonus.The room was lovely, very clean, king size bed, minibar (for which the prices were very reasonable), kettle, bathrobe and slippers. I had pre-ordered a bottle of Cava to be brought to the room and this was delivered within 5 mins of being shown to the room. It did take us a few minutes to work out how the shower worked and it was a day before we realised there was an aircon control in the cupboard. The room became stiffling hot and we thought the aircon was not working. We called recepton and someone was at the door within 2 minutes to show us how to work the aircon unit.The breakfast was divine, there was so much to chose from although I wouldn't be able to justify paying 18 euros each so thankfully this was incuded in the rate we paid for the room.Our only real critisism is the cost of the drinks in the bar. Yes you expect them to be on the expensive side but 25 euros for 2 glasses of sangria is a bit on the steep side and we didn't order any more drinks in the bar after that. Also there is a distict lack of English TV channels. Dont get me wrong, we weren't there to watch TV, but a couple of nights were shattered after all the walking we did and it would have been nice to go back and chill in the room after dinner and watch a film.Other than that, we cannot fault this hotel and when we go back to Barcelona we will definately stay here again.

<Author>MissHappy
<Content>Fantasic. No Complaints We have recently returned from a 2 night stay at the Hotel 1898. Wow the pictures on the website don't do it justice. It is spotless, clean, the staff are friendly and helpful. We had a superior room, decorated beautifully with a lovely terrace with table and chairs - extremely peaceful given the location. The spa is fab and a great way to refresh yourself after a hard day sightseeing. Would definitely recommend this hotel however as advised would try and get a BB rate for our return stay as the breakfast was 19 euros each. The breakfast was great with plenty to eat so you could always go back for seconds which we did. Sightseeing we would recommend the red hop on hop off bus and would get a 2 day ticket. If the weather is nice, definitely go for a boat trip, we did the port trip for 35 minutes as limited for time but should really have done the full 1.5 hour tour including port and coastline - much more interesting. Fabulous hotel and have recommended it to 2 friends in work who are interested.

<Author>trustytravellerFrome
<Content>Fantastic hotel with a great spa A lovely hotel which couldn't be more central but was still lovely and quiet. The spa and roof top pool really make this hotel and are just what you need after a long days sightseeing.Our room was comfy, spacious enough and the bathroom had a great huge rainwater shower head and bathrobe, slippers, nice toiletries etc. The only downside of the room was a rather dingy view over the back streets rather than the rambla that we were hoping for but it was nice and quiet probably because of this.A few eating out tips - Bar Ra behind the market is great for breakfast (as is the market itself), the bar next to the hotel is FAB and you can dance until 3am but don't eat in the Taxidermista restaurant (it was in our guide book as recommended but we thought it was terrible). Also despite what everyone says about the pick pockets we felt really safe although we were careful and didn't use the underground; we used the open top buses to get around as you can jump on and off as many times as you like. The bus from the airport was great too (only @ 4 euros) and dropped us off in Placa Catalunya which was only 5 mins from the hotel.All in all a great 3 day break!

<Author>KLS07
<Content>Great Memories Great advice helped me select Hotel 1898 for my 11 year old son and I for a weekend in Barcelona. Location is fabulous. Walked straight out onto La Ramblas. A few doors up a supermarket catered well for our late night snack urges and the metro line was 5 minutes walk.The hotel though was excellent. The Classic room was sufficient in size and had enough gadgets with the lighting, TV and bathroom set up to impress an 11 year old lad!There were a lot of couples there, and I would definitely take my wife for a romantic weekend. The bar area was pleasant and the rooftop bar looked great, although it was never open for service due to the weather. I imagine in the summer it would be a tremendous place to unwind after a day's sight-seeing.Reception staff were really helpful, but I didn't ask them for enough help. Once I did I was surprised how easy it was to get around the city via metro.Quick advice if you stay:If you use the basement spa and pool (which is great) get changed in your room and go down via the lift in your room's bathrobe as there are no real changing rooms to speak of.The breakfast is an extra 鈧?9 for the buffet which I felt was overpriced, particularly as when we arrived later in the morning it didn't look too appetising. In hindsight we could have used any number of cafes along La Ramblas and around the area.Get on the rooftop for sunset when you can get some great views of the city and in particular the Cathedral.Anyway, we enjoyed the hotel but then I haven't had the credit card bill yet!

<Author>Knowledgebuilders
<Content>1898 - Luxury and winter swimming One of our best hotel experiences ever. A well-heated rooftop pool meant good swimming even in chilly December. As far as we could tell, this is the only hotel in central Barcelona that provides this. With a comfortable large room on the next-to-top floor (room 610) it was like having a large pool and terrace for ourselves. Very helpful staff. There is considerable variation among rooms within a class, so try to get a look at the possibilities or discuss them with the staff. Contrary to what Expedia was saying, superior rooms don't have balconies or terraces. They are the same as standard rooms except for an outside view. The next grade up from superior, which we took (can't remember what it's called) gets you a considerably larger and nicely appointed room.

<Author>RoamInStyle
<Content>Great hotel, some buts... We stayed at 1898 for New Year and the week afterwards.It's a great hotel with many plus points, but there are one or two things to be aware of, see below.Pro's:- great location, at the top of La Rambla within walking distance of many of the main sights including much of the Gaudi architecture - Casa Battlo, Casa Mila and Sagrada Familia, also very near La Boqueria - a fantastic food market, and close to other great shopping around Placa Catalunya-impressive building, impressive bedrooms and bathrooms - all constantly being kept clean- great facilities - good gym (bikes, running machines, some weights) very, very stylish indoor pool with adjacent steam room and sauna, along with spa facitlities. Free wi-fi access in the rooms along with an internet centre on the first floor with a couple of desktops and printers- roof top terrace with outdoor pool - open all year and all evening with great views of the city - this is one of the best things about the hotel - a real oasis away from the hussle and bussle of La Rambla and warm enough in the sun to enjoy at this time of year- many nearby cafes, bakeries, wine shops and supermarketsCon's:- and this is the biggest con - rooms on the second floor at the back of the hotel are noisy. Yes, the rooms are soundproofed so you don't really hear noise outside or other guests, BUT there is a bar and nightclub - Bar Lobo - in the same building as the hotel. Rooms on the second floor at the back are directly above it's dancefloor and the structure of the building very effectively channels through the sound of the music. Bear in mind that the Spaniards love to party from midnight to around 4am, and if you are in one of these rooms, and are noise sensitive, you are going to be kept awake particularly on Friday and Saturday nights. The hotel obviously have complaints about the noise regularly, as when we complained there were a set of stock answers we were given. However on one particularly bad night they did move us to another room to sleep for the night. Request a quiet room on one of the higher floors when booking.- don't bother asking the front desk for restaurant recommendations - it's not there speciality. A good option for tapas is Taller de Tapas - they have two restaurants within walking distance of the hotel. For Paella, Can Majo is a good choice on the sea front - 40 mins walk or 10 mins taxi (鈧?0).- irons and ironing boards are not available. There is an ironing service, but taking a travel iron is probably easier.- there are tea and coffee making facilities in the rooms, but no milk. You can get milk in the nearby Carrefour supermarket (also great for buying bottles of Cava / Rioja)- 鈧?8 for breakfast - this is steep if you just want somethinbg small for breakfast. Around the back of the hotel (turn left past Bar Lobo) there is a deli/cafe that the locals go to, which serves great pastries and hot chocolate at a fraction of the price. There is also a good bakery if you continue past the back entrance of Carrefour.In summary, it's fantastic hotel in a great location, but steer clear of those rooms on the second floor at the back.  
<Date>Jan 6, 2007

<Author>LKP-VA
<Content>Even the cheapest room ("Classic") was great! We stayed here based on TripAdvisor reviews, and we were not disappointed! It is a beautiful hotel, with nice, helpful staff, and located very conveniently on La Rambla, up near the hub of the Plaza Catalunya. We arrived exhausted from our flight, and were shown to our room (we booked their cheapest room, a Classic). It was beautiful, quiet and comfortable, facing onto the beautiful interior courtyard, and we had a pleasant nap before setting out later to explore Barcelona. We also visited (but ultimately did not use) the downstairs spa (it was a little too popular!), and its pool is in a grotto that is unusual and pretty. We also went to the rooftoop, where their outdoor pool was open and heated (some were swimming in it, but the December night air was a little too chilly for us!). Both locations were beautiful and well appointed for relaxation.The day we left, we were able to leave our luggage with their front desk while we explored the city a little more, and the staff was very helpful in our decision as to how to get back to the airport.I would definitely stay here again if ever in Barcelona (Barcelona, by the way, was the highlight of our trip to Spain). A very good experience.Lisa from Williamsburg

<Author>UKMuffy
<Content>Would definitely stay again! Have just returned from a fantastic 2 night stay at Hotel 1898. It is in an ideal location, right in the middle of Las Ramblas. Originally we had booked a superior room, but saw the rooms below had decked terraces, so asked if we could change, and it was no problem. For 45 EUR extra per night we were shown to a huge room, with a big terrace with 4-seater table, and a raised double daybed. It was warm enough to have breakfast on the terrace both days. The bathroom was a great size, with hugh bath, and a separate shower. This room was definitely worth the extra money, for a special treat!The spa facilities are great. The pool is under a brick archway, and is very atmospherically lit. Along with the sauna and steamroom, they also have a water massage bed which is free for guests to use, and it was a real bonus after a day of pounding the pavements of Barcelona!The staff were really helpful, and always seemed to be there when you needed them, but faded into the background when you didn't. Our room was tidied and cleaned when we got back from sightseeing, and the bed was turned down each night whilst we were in the spa.Bar Lobos, round the back of the hotel, was fabulous for drinks and tapas on saturday night, but there was an hour wait for a table inside. That was fine though - we just decided to take our drinks and eat outside. I would definitely stay here again, for the very central location, the level of service, the lovely room, and the spa facilities.
