<Author>Beverstone
<Content>Highly recommended for an elegant stay (Member in Surrey, UK) We were in Barcelona for three nights. Since we had booked the opera, the 1898 (being such a short walking distance from the Liceu) was an obvious choice. We found it to be a highly elegant, modern and friendly hotel. And was excellent value when compared with the high prices often charged here in the UKBut there are a couple of points prospective visitors might like to keep in mind. Firstly the breakfast is not cheap. But if you intend to have a really good meal to see you through much of the day, then I certainly recommend it. But if, like me, you prefer a very light snack you could do better to go along the road towards the Liceu and enjoy a coffee and an excellent pastry for a fraction of the cost. Also the bar is expensive and not good. We paid a high price for our dry martini (which we didn't object to given the status of the hotel) but it was not a particularly good one (being too ice-melt diluted) and came without any customary cocktail 'nibbles' that enhance the occasion and one could expect at this price. So having a drink was a rather 'triste' experience , which we certainly did not repeat.

I'd suggest this hotel is a solid 3 1/2 star (would be a 4 if they took some of the details up a notch).

<Author>mspw
<Content>Lives up to the good reviews Thankfully the other reviews of this hotel have largely been accurate. I stayed there in early September in a superior room for a week and was not disappointed (overall). Highlights: 1: Decent rooms (but I was glad I followed other reviewers' advice to book a superior room - it costs more for a reason - its usually a room on the outside of the hotel as opposed to the smaller standard rooms overlooking the inner atrium. The standard rooms' dark walls and small dimensions suffer further from the dingy atrium that restricts most of the natural light). Our room was at the back of the hotel with a balcony overlooking a cafe - not a great view, but pleasant and much quieter than those overlooking the Ramblas. 2: Decent Spa in the basement. Not great when kids were allowed in (supervised), but very quiet in the mornings and early afternoons. The pool wasn't very large (the picture on the hotel's own web-site was accurate), and could do with being warmer, but it was ok in conjunction with the steam room and sauna and there were several spa treatments available. 3: Very nice roof terrace. Although the pool was unheated and you needed to get there early (late afternoon) to grab a large sofa or four-poster bed sun lounger on the west side of the building to catch the last of the sun. 4: 24 hour internet access - albeit in the business centre on the 1st floor. Lowlights: 1: Variable customer service - usually very pleasant but hardly overeager. They have a concierge service but nowhere near the level of service of some other hotels (although this is after all only four star) - they were fairly unenthusiastic when asked to phone a restaurant to tell them we were delayed; and room service also seemd a bit put out about being called after they had overlooked re-supplying tea and coffee! Having said that, I did ask them to arrange for flowers, wine and fruit to be in our room on arrival, which they did, and I was never charged !(surely a mistake). 2: The hotel food was hardly much to rave about. The hotel breakfast is only worth the price if you can eat your weight in breakfast items - we found it much better and infinitely cheaper to buy anything we wanted in the supermarket over the road from the side entrance of the hotel. 3: Availability of food and drinks on the roof terrace was limited. Again, the opening hours of the bar varied a great deal and you were better off taking your own drinks and food up there - a bit of a hassle in a four star hotel! 4: You had to call room service for hot water or milk and there no irons were provided, only an ironing service - ok if you trust your clothes to someone else, but far from convenient when you're in a rush to get out - suffice to say the travel kettle and iron other reviwers advised came in really handy!Those gripes aside, the hotel is very well located, even if the Ramblas is a little tacky. We had no hassles from any beggars, and never felt unsafe at any time of the day or night even though we were often returning at 3 or 4 am. Overall, the hotel was well worth the money which is probably why its so popular even though its not a 5 star hotel. Having seen other hotels I was about to book - Casa Camper (dark, dingy and inhospitable!) and Hotel Neri, where I popped in for a few drinks as friends were staying there, I was not disappointed.A few Barcelona recommendations: Breakfast in the cafes at the rear of the hotel (on Carrer del Carme); great tapas at, Taller de Tapas near Santa Maria del Mar church, and even better pancakes around the corner on Passeig del Born. Clubs: Danzatoria in Tibidabo (food and wine was really good although expensive, the club attracts a well-heeled 20 to 30 crowd and is spread over a garden area and several floors of a mansion type house, with a pretty wide range of music (for Spain!)), Shoko is a bit more low rent as its in the Port Olimpic area on the beachfront, but is one of the better clubs there. Club 13 / Tarantos in Placa Real was a lot grittier, but the live bands and largely local crowd make it well worth a visit. Try the web-site [--] for more. Idling away a few hours (or days) in el Born's boutique antique, gift and clothes shops was fantastic, as was visiting Gaudi's Sagrada Familia and Casa Mila, but I would avoid the more touristy shops and restaurants on the Ramblas (including Attic restaurant across the road from the hotel - it comes recommended by some but the service and food was pretty poor quality), as well as any restaurant on Carrer de la Princesa (poor quality overpriced seafood) or anywhere in Port Olimpic (although if you want a quick snack at a subway or Pizza Hut Port Olimpic is the place to go!!) The Maremagnum shopping centre in Port Vell is also full of tacky gifts and high street rubbish. Cabs are not too expensive, but the metro was ideal - it was cleaner, cheaper and more frequent than the london tube and usually quicker than a cab if you don't mind not seeing the sights as you travel. The 3 official guided bus tours that start from Placa de la Catalunya are also well worth a try. If you have time, a tour on each takes around 2-3 hours or so, and you get to see virtually everything you need.  
<Date>Oct 17, 2006

<Author>pedro3gb
<Content>Great Hotel in best location A 5 minute walk from the airport bus stop leads you to this new hotel at the top end of The Ramblas - right opposite Le Meridien. On entering by the revolving door you notice the beautifully stylish sofas and chairs in herringbone and stiped fabrics. The decor may be classed as 'historic' on the nn website but its not at all old fashioned or chintzy. The reception staff are friendly and helpful and carried out little tasks such as charging a run down mobile phone.The main lobbly is also brilliantly stylish with loads of seating, artwork, model ships in cases etc. Rooms are something else and everything is high quality. The floors are solid mahoghany and green marble in the bathroom, matt laquered wardrobes and doors, double twin bed with a selection of four different types of pillows, bathrobes and slippers and a wide selection of quality toiletries, even totthbrushes, paste, shavers, and shaving cream.Coffees and teas were provided but if you want hot water and milk you have to ring room service. You do get a silver flask full of hot water with silver jug of milk within about 5 minutes.We did not take breakfast in the hotel as $18 is quite expensive if you eat small breakfasts but all around are great cafes where you can get a perfectly adequate one for under $5. Farrgi is a good bet for this. Alternatively try one of the half slices of paw paw, dragon fruit or mango wrapped with spoon from thye market just down the street.The bar, like many hotel bars was quiet and two whiskies came to $14 - not excessive bearing in mind the quantity you get in Spanish establishments.This hotel seems to be the same price with every booking agency so not worth shopping around.

<Author>azazaz
<Content>Hotel 1898 vs Monte Carlo THE BEST BARCELONA HOTEL! Stayed at Hotel Monte Carlo 3 days pre-cruise and 1 post cruise night at Hotel 1898. Hotel 1898 wins hands down. I wish we'd booked this hotel for all of our days in Barcelona. I'm very particular where I stay and I could not find one thing I'd change about the comfort and convenience offered. The rooms were much smaller than Monte Carlo but it was large enough to meet our needs. We were in a premium room with a small balcony that overlooked Las Ramblas and there was absolutely NO street noise when the balcony door was closed. I did see some interior rooms that were very small so booking premium for a few dollars more is definitely worth it.I don't understand how Le Meridian gets away with charging so much more for their rooms when 1898 is directly across the street for so much less.We ate dinner at their restaurant one night and it was definitely gourmet quality, a little expensive but the ambience made it well worth it. The drinks on the rooftop patio were around 12E each, but they were large enough to qualify for two drinks and they did not skimp on the alcohol. There is also topless sunbathing so if you're offended avoid it. Can't wait to go back to BCN and I now know which hotel choice we'll be making in hotels if we ever get the opportunity to return.

<Content>Fantastic The Hotel 1898 is probably the best hotel I have ever stayed at. Great location and impressive facilities - from the room, to the lobby and bar, to the rooftop pool and basement spa! Would definately recommend this hotel and stay here again when in Barcelona!

<Author>mrgekko
<Content>Really Impressive My wife and I stayed at the 1898 at the start of October 2006. It's a fantastic hotel - in many respects a 5* experience, though perhaps falling short of an official rating on one or two technicalities. Things that you may find useful when considering booking are : * Roof Terrace - Gloriously quiet with panoramic views of the city, nice bar, but no food. (note you can zip out and get a salad in 5 minutes and bring it back without any eyebrows raised!)*Concierge - are very efficient and booked us into some unbookable restaurants at short notice (including Moo which is a must if you want to indulge!). Also left a note in our room confirming this had been done* Location - is possibly as good as it gets. You can pretty much get anywhere you need with ease. Bus-service reliable and easy to work out. We explored a lot and the only cabs we got were to and from the airport. * Agree with the earlier post about the noise from the maids which is quite loud (but the earliest we heard was 9.00am and our room was right opposite one of their base rooms). The rooms were spotless though. * Spa - Pool small but fun, sauna and steam rooms both fine, clean etc. Again if you want to indulge massages were very good. * Price - in response to the other poster who said that the hotel charges for everything, i'm a little surprised. True that there is no kettle in the room but my wife and I asked a few times at the bar for hot water and milk which was provided for no extra cost. Maybe it was the room service delivery element that caused them to be charged. Also, breakfast cost is pretty competitive for a hotel of this standard and of good quality. I've stayed in similar hotels across the continent where a similar spread has been a lot more expensive. Overall, this place is highly recommended and all the positive reviews below, which prompted us to book, are spot on! Enjoy!  
<Date>Oct 5, 2006

<Author>GavandClaire
<Content>Fantastic!!!!!! We have just returned from a 3 night stay at Hotel 1898 and have to say that the hotel lived up to all of our expectations after reading the reviews.It was most definitely more 5 star than 4 star with the rooftop pool and day beds being a very luxurious feature and the views from there- WOW! and at 165euros a night was a bargain!The room was spacious ( we stayed in room 308) and although a little dark ( it being a coutyard view room) it was very quiet and pleasant- peace and tranquility away from the hustle and bustle of the Ramblas.The bathroom was fabulous with a great shower ( the biggest shower head I have ever seen) and plenty of towels, bathrobes, slippers and complementary toiletries.The bed was huge and comfortable and the different lighting very relaxing after a hard days sightseeing,eating and drinking.The only criticism I have is that we requested an iron but were advised that they only offer a laundry service.The indoor pool, gym and steam room/sauna were more than adequate.We chose not to eat in the hotel instead opting for the many resaurants/ Tapas bars and market nearby.Breakfast - the market for its choice of fresh fruit and a very handy starbucks next door.Dinner- Dont eat til late -10pm earliest. We tried many restauarants but one of our favourites was 'set portes- passeig d'isabel ll 14'. Its been there since 1836 and has queues out the door so you have to book. The paella was delicious.Will definitely stay again at the 1898 - a real treat!

Decoration is hip, the atmosphere is not. So it is recommended, but do not expect 5 star service, they do not make the extra mile. High potential though!

<Author>Out-of-SFO
<Content>Great New Hotel We just spent three nights at 1898 and were very pleased in all respects. As it is located on La Rambla, we were concerned about noise and had therefore requested an interior standard room. We were shown to our room on the third of six floors, which had two large outward opening windows overlooking a small inner courtyard with potted plants at the base. Because of that, the room was a little darker than exterior rooms or those exterior with terraces, but we preferred that over potential street noise. Location was great, though in a very touristy area. You can walk to all of the main points of interest, and we did not have any trouble hailing a cab either. One real bonus is the Boquiera Market, which is about a block further down La Rambla -- incredible outdoor covered market for meats, seafood, fruits, bar-style restaurants. We bought some food there and brought it back to the room one day. Do watch for pick pockets there and on La Rambla generally, as you would in any highly congested area where it is easy to get distracted by all of the goings on. Spain overall felt very safe, certainly safer than large cities in the US, but like anywhere petty crimes of opportunity will occur. The hotel occupies what was formerly the headquarters for Compania de Tabacos de Filipinas, which was built in 1881. It was completely redone 8 months ago and provides an interesting mix of very modern high-end furnishing and wall treatments but the original fascade, high ceilings (in rooms too) and ornate details. Because it is so new, it has not yet been written up in the guidebooks; however, I expect that when the new editions come out that this hotel will be right at the top. While we paid 150 euros per night without breakfast, a room of our standard room's quality combined with the overall luxe feel of the hotel and its full range of amenities would easily fetch $350-450/night in San Francisco or New York.The rooftop deck, which has a very modern lounge-y feel with built-ins and other freestanding seating areas, is lovely with views out over the city in all directions. It was especially welcome in the evenings during our stay becauses it was so hot during the day. The pool located on rooftop is on the small side, but nice for cooling off and lazing around. On the floor below the streel-level reception desk is another pool/spa facility, which is pretty amazing. Apparently the stone and brickwork arched ceiling over that pool is part of the original building and was uncovered during the renovation. It feels like you are in ancient roman bath or a wine cave, but the new pool itself, which is larger than the rooftop pool, has jacuzzi jets, two overhanging waterfall type fixtures, and two stainless steel lounge chairs that are submerged in the water with pinhole jets in the backs/seats. There is an adjacent steam room and sauna, as well as a glass enclosed air-conditioned exercise room with treadmill, etc. Plenty of towels, water, changing facilities, etc. All of the above is free to hotel guests. The rooms were handsomely decorated (peeked in a few others while being cleaned), complete with large plasma tvs with good array of English channels, in-room music system, and room lighting that allows you to dim the lights to various levels at the touch of a button (modes: welcome, relax, reading, nighttime). The bathroom was all forest green marble with both hand-held shower hose and rainfall showerhead. It was initally a bit confusing to figure out how to go from tub faucet, to hand-held, to rainfall mode. There is a towel warming rack, which was great for laundry. Plenty of toiletries, hair dryer, etc. In closet safe, fridge, etc. I couldn't, however, get an iron when I inquired about it, though they did have laundry service. They offer pillow service as well, which I tried. The room came equipped with hypoallergenic synthetic pillows, two each: one longer bolster-type and then one larger European square pillow. The card in the room offers several other pillows, including down and memory foam. We tried those two, and the housekeeping staff left the originals as well, so we could go back and forth between them. As others have noted, the rooms have two twins pushed together, which does appear to be common in Spain. It makes for spacious king, but isn't ideal. Air conditioning, which we needed worked very well. However, there was a consistent intermittent mild bonking noise, which we finally realized only occurred when the air was on. I would imagine that it was specific to our room, and it wasn't a big deal. There is a large, nicely decorated computer room -- think clubby with sofas, music, great lighting, magazines while you wait. There are two computers with printers, all free of charge. There is no concierge to speak of, though the reception desk attempts to fill that roll. The front desk employees' affect could afford to be a bit more friendly, but they weren't actually negative or surely. I guess I would summarize their mode as slightly cool. Overall, one of the nicest hotels that I have stayed in; hip but not at the expense of comfort. I'd definitely go back and highly recommend it. I wish that every city that I visit had a hotel as nice as this one and at similar rates. While there are three rooms with private pools on the corners of the fifth floor, and others with private terraces, I wouldn't hesitate to stay in a standard interior room as we did, as the overall hotel amenities are so wonderful that you will be very happy with the communal outdoor areas. The hotel is not cuurently very busy from what I can gather, which I think is due to the fact that it is so new. It would an overnight success in Manhattan or LA, or any urban setting in the US for that matter. Best way to book, according to the hotel, is as we did, through their website nnhotels.es. They have several hotels in Barcelona, including Hotel Jazz, which is also highly rated by tripadvisor reviewers. We saw it as we were riding by in a cab one day, but did not actually go in.  
<Date>Aug 3, 2006

<Author>LyndaMacdonald
<Content>Close to perfection in Barcelona This must surely be amongst the very best hotels in Barcelona. My boyfriend (a hotel snob it must be said) booked this weekend away as a surprise and boy did he earn brownie points for this hotel. Only about 15 minutes from the airport means it's perfect for short stays. Situated just off La Rambla we had reservations that it would be noisy - we couldn't hear a thing when the doors were closed. Our room had a private terrace and I think it is definitely worth the extra expense for that - it meant we had our (fantastic but quite expensive) breakfasts sitting in our own private dining room outside. I reckon room 528 must be the best though as it has it's own pool and is on a corner site - next time...I used the air-conditioned gym (sad I know!) each morning and the cellar pool is just heaven (although respect to anyone who actually manages to recline in the spa loungers in the pool). I appreciated the free bottled water and towels downstairs too. The pool on the roof is also just heaven - need a few more loungers but the views are fantastic and the extra breeze up there is very welcome. Would like to have seen them serve food on the roof terrace as they do have the tables and chairs for it but at the moment it's just bar service. Our room was immaculate and the bathroom was very cool (I'm a huge fan of a good bathroom!) - shower is confusing at first but we got the hang of it after a while. Air-conditioning is the quietest I've ever experienced and works brilliantly. Daily maid service was excellent and it's worth noting that the mini-bar prices are not silly so you don't feel too guilty at raiding it. I would have preferred a double bed rather than two beds put together but then I'm British so we like that kind of thing. Couldn't really fault this hotel at all - if I could go back tomorrow I would - it's a slice of heaven in a very cool city. The only you'd change about Barcelona is to make the shop and waiting staff friendlier - they all appear a little off-ish and stressed and I speak Spanish so they don't have that excuse! If you get the chance go to Hotel 1898 - I'll be hugely jealous.

<Author>mogstown
<Content>Highly recommended! We spent an excellent three nights at this hotel last weekend, which I chose based on the recommendations from this website, and I have to say, we were not disappointed!I had booked us a deluxe room (direct with the hotel through their website) which certainly had a wow factor, and an amazing private terrace (about the same size as our bedroom) from the double doors in our room. The view from the terrace (we were on the fifth floor) was great and there were table and chairs, and padded benches to sit on and laze around. We requested a bottle of champagne in our room for arrival, and this was done without any fuss, they even sent me the champagne list in advance so that I could choose.The room was lovely, the bathroom fantastic, believe everything everyone is saying about the shower - absolutely great, nothing like anything I've seen in the UK. The lighting in the room was also very good with four levels of lighting available.Despite others' comments, we did have breakfast in the hotel on two mornings. I felt that it compared very well in price to the breakfasts in full service hotels in the UK, and there was a great variety in the buffet (though the cakes looked a little rich for that early in the morning!!) The concierge was very helpful in supplying us with a map of Barcelona, even going so far as to point out which roads to avoid in the midday sun, and which ones had the best shade.We did have a slight issue with the bar service on the Saturday evening. Before we went out to eat, we thought it would be nice to have a drink in the bar, but the bar team member did not acknowledge us, and we waited, and even though he was attending to someone else, he did not even acknowledge us, or smile, or say hello, so we decided to go somewhere with a little more friendliness and warmth.The only other issue we had was on our last night, when we could hear running water, and so we couldn't sleep. The night porter came to our room, and heard the noise, but was unable to solve the problem (still not sure what it was, could have been coming from room above?) but he did offer us a room move, but as we were checking out in the morning, we declined. He handled it well, but no mention of a reduction in the rate to compensate our wakeful night.Still, we did love this hotel, the roof terrace is great, with fantastic views, and a good opportunity to relax after walking around a very hot Barcelona. Towels are supplied, so just bring your bathing suit.The location of the hotel is excellent, and we would recommend it to anyone looking to be pampered. I'd recommend the deluxe level room which was very good. We'd go again, and we're hoping to visit this lovely hotel and fabulous city again later this year.

<Content>Sensational!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect hotel - we loved every minute! We have just returned from a perfect five night break to Barcelona. It was our first trip to the city and Hotel 1898 had been recommended us. We booked directly through the hotel (the availability was far better than on various travel websites) and the price was great too. From the minute we arrived we were delighted with our choice. We couldn't fault anything about the hotel. We were upgraded on arrival and our room was fantastic - full of small touches to make it extra special. We didn't eat our meals in the hotel but made full use of all the rest of the facilities, all of which were above expectation. We spent early evenings relaxing on the huge sunbeds by the roof top pool with its fanastic views and had a massage, sauna and swim in the basement spa - again the service was impeccable and the little touches - sunlounge style jacuzzi chairs in the pool, waterfall showers - made all the difference.The location is ideal for exploring all of the main tourist areas - the metro is a 2 minute walk, although we walked nearly everywhere. The hotel is so quiet you wouldn't know you were on the main tourist drag. I am not a fan of major tourist areas but La Ramblas is great for people watching and street shows (although I would not eat anywhere - there are far nicer restaurants not far away down the side streets). The hotel is extremely reasonably priced for what are more than 4 star facilities and service. We loved every minute of our stay at Hotel 1898 - we will definitely be returning to Barcelona and wouldn't even consider staying anywhere else.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect hotel for a relaxing weekend My wife and I have just returned from a 3-day trip to Barcelona, and couldn't rate the H1898 highly enough. We have been to Barcelona several times before but this was our first trip to this hotel -- we won't be staying anywhere else in future as you won't find a better hotel for the price.The best bits:* The roof terrace -- very stylishly put together, with sun loungers, a bar, a (small) pool and lots of other seating, including two large double-bed sized mattresses perfect for soaking up the sun on* The pool in the spa in the basement. A superb setting in a converted cellar, with free use also of the gym, steam room and sauna - a relaxing way to end the trip and grab a shower before jumping on the plane if you have an evening flight* It's a brand new hotel, so everything is pristine -- no lumpy pillows or bashed light fittings here* The location -- right on Las Ramblas, but very few rooms actually overlook the road so is isn't noisy. It's situated near the top of the Ramblas opposite Le Meridien -- 5 mins from Plaza Catalunya, the metro system, El Corte Ingles and the airport bus stopWhat types of people you'll see there:* Couples in their mid 30s-mid 50s* Well-heeled groups of twentysomethings* Business peopleWe booked a corner room (if you're booking online it's the room with red furnishings rather than black) which was a little bigger than a standard room and becaise it was on a corner had an extra window. Would probably book a standard room next time, although judging by the relative size of the rooms on the fire exit plan they look fairly compact.We didn't try room service (there are too many good tapas bars around) -- the only thing we'd change is to provide coffee and tea-making facilities in the room. Tea is complementary, but you need to call down for hot water.In case you're hungry there are loads of good tapas bars around, and the restaurant on the 1st floor of the building opposite the hotel on Las Ramblas called The Attic is excellent.Enjoy your stay!

<Author>waterstone
<Content>Quiet, clean hotel, centrally located I spent 5 nights here at the end of June/early July, in a superior room without breakfast included. The room was large and looked out on what appeared to be an alleyway. I believe there was some sort of small restaurant with a patio there, and there was occasional noise as a result. However, it was generally very quiet, and I'm not especially worried about the view. The furnishings and decor are contemporary, though the materials used seem fairly simple.There was a very comfortable king-size bed with nice linens and various pillows to choose from. To their credit, hotel management has installed hardwood floors in the entryway and main room. Air conditioning was excellent and the closet was large. There was a flat-panel wall-mounted LCD TV. The lighting, in its various settings, can be controlled from the bed.The bathroom is nicely done in green stone and was very roomy. Huge towels, constantly replenished toiletries (including toothbrush/toothpaste, razor/shaving cream, and the usual other supplies), plush bathrobes and disposable slippers were provided. The showerhead is about the size of a dinner plate and water pressure and temperature were excellent.There is a restaurant which is really not too bad. I had dinner a couple of times and found the staff to be very pleasant and helpful. The food, while not wildly creative (go to Abac, Moo, Cinc Sentits, Comer莽 24, etc. for that), was tasty and featured good ingredients and simple preparations.I didn't spend a great deal of time interacting with the staff or using the spa. The lobby area is somewhat dark but tastefully decorated. Features of the old Compa帽铆a General de Tabacos de Filipinas building have been carefully preserved.I would recommend this hotel to my friends and colleagues. The client猫le wasn't upper crust (if that matters to you), and there seemed to be a number of small tour groups booked in as well. I only hope that the current standard of the hotel will be maintained.

Needless to say the maitre de stopped the waiter and asked why we were leaving and hey presto we got a table in the window. <Author>Sunshine World Traveller
<Content>Oasis of delight I stayed with my boyfriend in this hotel in May for 3 nights and we were both very impressed. Both of us travel quite alot and have stayed in 5 star hotels on numerous occasions. Hotel 1898 is every bit as good as any 5 star hotel and was magical from the moment we stepped into the foyer - very modern unique chic decor. The Charlie Chaplin slient movies playing on the LCD screen in the lobby is a novelle idea. We had a delux room on the 3rd floor that overlooked the street, as the windows were sound proofed we never heard any traffic at night. Although satellite TV, Sky News was about the only chanel in english. Bathroom was very large with beautiful marble work - bathrobe and slippers for both of us and they were very generous with restocking the toiletries every day. Down side if you want to have a tea or coffee you must order the hot water and as is often the case in warm climates - it wasn't very hot! The staff were all very helpful and were always smiling and polite..The jacuzzi was wonderful, as was the indoor pool (although on the small side) and the sauna just perfect for relaxing on holiday.My boyfriend is a major Starbucks fan and was delighted to have one next door to the hotel - there's even a Dunken Doughnuts open 24 hrs a day a few doors down. Breakfast is definitely best from the market - again only 3 min walk from the hotel. Ours tended to be an unhealthy mix of delicious fruits and decadent chocolates!!Hotel is in a central location right on Las Rambles - within 10 min walk of the port area and only 2 mins from Placa Cataluyna where you can get a hop-on-hop-off city tour bus every 10 mins. Great way to get initial feel for the city. Shops were also in 3-5min walking distance of hotel. Would definitely recommend hotel and would love to return to it soon again - however I fear it will become very popular and the prices may increase too.

<Author>Scaggers
<Content>Chic, calm, haven I stayed at this hotel with my partner for 3 nights over the May bank holiday weekend. The hotel is in a fantastic location on La Rambla and within walking distance of the port / beach. Despite it's lively location the interior of the hotel is calm, cool and chic - an oasis in the madness. The decor is modern and tasteful - all dark wood and monochrome with splashes of red - but has character as it has retained a lot of the period features during it's conversion. The rooms are a moderate size and everything is extremely clean.We went to the hotel wanting a relaxing pamper and weren't disappointed. The basement of the hotel has an indoor pool with jacuzzi and a sauna / spa / gym area. The roof of the hotel has an outdoor pool and numerous sunbathing areas with cushions (big enough for two). We didn't manage to eat in the restaurant (there was too much choice outside) but the hotel bar was a great place for aperitifs.I would definitely stay there again and would recommend this hotel for anyone wanting a romantic or relaxing break.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel 1898 was the best part of Barcelona I hate to say this, but Barcelona isn't my favorite place in Europe, but the Hotel 1898 is my favorite hotel in Europe. WOW! this place is great. The people are wonderful, especially helping me out with my rusty Spanish. The rooms were great, the hallway could be a bit noisy, but the bathroom was superb. Could have stayed in the shower all day. The roof top pool wasn't open, but Eduardo who works downstairs in the bar snuck us up on the roof around 10PM. It will be open on May 22, 2006. What a view. He also showed us the penthouse suites, if anyone can afford it $1500 eur a night, they are beautiful with their own private pool and deck. The only thing I can say that wasn't great was the massage. My friend and I both had a massage in their spa. The gentleman was very nice, recommended a great tapas restaurant which we ate at almost everyday. Txelapia, or something like that. Anyway, back to the massage. It was very soft, not a massage I'm used to in the States. Plus, and I don't know if this is an American thing, but this isn't for the modest. I was fully exposed most of the time. We complained to the manager and she comped us the charge. Like I said, maybe this is how they do massages in Europe. But, other than we had a fabulous stay. They is a Starbuck next door, but if you want the best capaccino ever, go to the hotel bar. It's pricey, but worth it. If I ever do decide to go back to Barcelona I will stay here again. Maybe I'll save my money and stay in the Penthouse Suite.  
<Date>May 14, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A must stay!! Stayed at the 1898 with my (gorgeous) girlfriend for three nights at the end of April.I booked due to other reviews on TA and wasn't dissapointed. The hotel itself is in a perfect location, at the (nicer) top end of La Ramblas. You are just a stones throw away from one of the open top buses main stations which will take you to all the major tourist attractions that the city has.The hotel itself is fantastic. The decor is very modern, it has the feel of a new hotel as soon as you come through the main doors. When we arrived by taxi from the airport we were greeted at the doors and our luggage carried in for us. The people on reception were very friendly and we were upgraded to a room with a veiw on to La Ramblas straight away. The room itself was quality, with a big plasma TV and the bathroom was gorgeous all green marble and very stylish. The shower head was the biggest I've ever seen and it was a treat to get back to after sightseeing for a day.The pool wasn't open on the roof but the one in the hotel itself was very nice. Dimly lit and very relaxing. The sauna and the steam room seemed fine as well but we didn't really use them that much.The hotel bar is great. The two blokes working behind it, Carlos  Eduardo were veryhospitable and good to have a laugh with (especially Carlos when you'd sunk a few beers), and the Sangira they made us was beutiful and strong!! The bar was a bit pricey but in my eyes your on holiday and should be treating yourself anyway.I wouldn't recommend eating on La Ramblas as it was pricey and the food wasn't that good but there are some great resteraunts located just off it.All in all we had a great time and when we come back will 100% be staying in the 1898.Thanks for a great time!!Tommy  Jerry

<Author>mmyk72
<Content>Great location, decor, clean I stayed here a week in March. I love the new feeling and cleaniness of this hotel. The decor and furnishing are very chic, new, and sleek but yet classic. My superior room was just like what the pictures show, with strong red color, hard wood floor, LCD tv, etc. The bathroom is awesome, but make sure someone shows you how the bath fixtures work since they took me 10 min to figure out.The location is perfect on the lively La Rambla, between 2 metro stops, and next to a supermarket and the Boqueria (fresh food market). One negative is that breakfast is not included despite the high room price. I think the hotel breakfast is 20 euros, and not many cafes around the hotel are open before 8 am.The service is great overall. However, there was some construction outside the hotel and the noise can be bothersome. On a Friday morning which I intented to sleep in, construction noise from what seemed to be from inside the building started at ~ 8:30 am. I called in to complain and the noise stopped for about 1 hr. This shows that the staff did care and overall service for the week had been in line for this class of hotel. However, having pounding sound early in the morning is quite unacceptable for a room costing $300 US a night.

<Author>maliblue
<Content>Amazing Gem My fiance and I just finished a 3 night stay at 1898 and was wonderfully suprised at every turn... the style of the hotel is fantastic, the service was top notch and the bathrooms made you look forward to a shower (I am not sure where all that water comes from...).. the underground pool is in what appears to be an old wine cave with water sculptures, it was beautiful.......the only suggestion I have is to make sure that you get an exterior room if you want to feel part of the city, the interior rooms look out upon a small courtyard of the hotel which is not unique. I have travelled extensively and stayed at hotels as varied as the burj al arab in dubai or the George V in Paris.. this hotel is not five star, but one of the nicest in town four stars you could find.....also, skip the breakfast as with most hotels in spain, it is better to take a walk down the street..... Try to attend and opera if that is your thing.. the opera is just around the corner. Also, there is a very modern and chic restaurant with great food just across the Ramlbas called Attic... stop by early or have the hotel call for reservations.....

I know it's probably more likely that a poor hotel/etc would warrant someone posting comment but I was so impressed with Hotel 1898 that the hotel deserved some more warranted praise.Ideal location on La Ramblas, the hotel is a new, nice looking hotel with courteous staff. The room was even cleaned twice a day- once at lunch and then another when we were out at night - never known that! Lovely shower (always a bug of mine when travelling, so often poor showers), plasma tv, comfortable bed - only thing I had a problem with is working out how to use/close the safe. Barca is a great city, and this booked through expedia was the perfect hotel. Best I've stayed in I'd go as far to say.

<Author>beentheredoneit
<Content>Excellent City Centre Hotel We stayed for 4 nights in March 2006, having carefully researched the available hotels we wanted a central location with facilities, pool, spa etc and 1898 did not disappoint. The location is superb, at the top end of Ramblas which is a bit like Barcelona's Covent Garden with street performers and artists making for a lively atmosphere. It is also a short walk to the more upmarket shopping areas and famous landmarks such as Gaudi's Casa Mila, and about 10 mins walk to the port at the bottom of Ramblas. 10/10 for the location.Some of the reviews mention poor service from the staff this was not out experience. All the staff were very friendly and attentive with an eye for detail such as welcoming us in English and by name. The service is however not overbearing, which we prefer, some may interpret this as a shortcoming and there is no concierge but the reception staff are excellent with good local knowledge.The rooms are extremely well appointed with wooden flooring, differing colour schemes, marble bathrooms with high quality Grohe fittings and nice touches such as heated mirrors in the bathroom that don't steam up!The basement pool and spa is a real plus. The pool has Jacuzzi areas, and is just big enough for a bit of a swim. A nice sauna, steam room and gym are also available and a treatment room, all of which was very tastefully finished and kept immaculately clean during our stay.A couple of minor points stopped this from becoming my favourite all time city center hotel (an accolade still held just by Hotel de Russie in Rome).We were woken by workmen in the next room to us laying flooring at 8.30 am, so whilst the room was well isolated from external noise it could not stop the sound of hammering from next door! Reception promptly moved us to a quieter room, but really we should not have been put in a room next to this work in the fist place.We were also disappointed to arrive back one night at exactly 1.00 AM to find the bar closed, despite the fact drinks were still being poured for other guests who had ordered before. A later conversation with the barman revealed a friendly guy, but one who definitely worked to rule! He was planning to come to work in London and was horrified when we told him how late London hotel bars stay open till!Our only experience of the food was a room service breakfast, the order got a bit mixed up, but was corrected very quickly and the food was excellent. When we checked out it had been missed off the bill, which I pointed out to reception who waived the charge for the breakfast. Our return flight was a late flight, and the manager agreed to a late check out and then stored our bags and valuables enabling us to enjoy a final look around the City.The Hotel has only been open since November 05, and I think it is a real find. I would not hesitate to recommend it, and look forward to going back in the summer when the roof terrace is open - where else would you be able to have the best of a beautiful city like Barcelona on your doorstep and then relax in the sun and swim as well?  
<Date>Apr 3, 2006

Very disappointing for a romantic break!

<Author>RobiOne
<Content>1898: a jewel on the noisy ramblas! We must admit that we selected the hotel after reading enthousiastic reviews from other people. We had not found a place in our first choice (Banys Orientals) and were almost falling in the trap of the fancy website of GAT RAVAL.Still, one of the reviews claimed 1898 was not at all a luxury hotel and staff was unhelpful so we were warned...Our experience was JUST PERFECT.As we arrived, we were upgraded to a superior room with no extra charge because all standards were taken.The room was tastefully decorated. Having myself worked in the building sector I particularly appreciated the choice of marbles, the quality of the parquet and the finishings.The air conditioning was not perfectly working, so they sent a person to fix it within minutes.Reception people were helpful and friendly (maybe because I am fluent in Spanish and we could exchange more)and the hotel very clean.The only negative thing we experienced was the room service, really too slow...If you can choose your room, prefer one that does not overlook the street: everybody knows the Spanish (but also the visitors of Barcelona!) like to celebrate and stay up late! The alternative is to bring your earplugs!We will definitely go back to this hotel, maybe even organize a business event there, because the facilities are brand new!

<Content>Perfect - really should be a 5* rather than a 4* Myself and my partner have just returned from Hotel 1898 for a 3 night stay from the 9th to the 12th of February. I've never actually written a review before however Tripadvisor was very helpful to me when choosing the hotel for a very special surprise weekend with my partner so I've decided to put our views in writing - so here goes!From the outset there was somebody to help with the bags and the staff were very professional, polite and helpful taking us up to the room and even showing us how to use the lights (a very cool and modern dimmer system) and the bathrooms (all Ghroe fittings with a fantastic rainfall shower). The decor was perfect, rooms had plenty of room and nice and quiet (no noise from the hallway hardwood floors as suggested by some - all carpeted). Our room had a brand new 32 LCD TV mounted on the was which was very nice and the aircon was spot on. Breakfast was amazing (I echo what another reviewer said though - get it included in the price or its 拢18 euro a day each). The pool and sauna faclilities were very nice and very quiet also. We spent a fair bit of time at the hotel bar after an evening out chating to Carlos the happy little barman (he makes great and very potent - Sangria which we recomend!) Location - halfway down La Ramblas (directly opposite the Meridian) was perfect.Somebody made a comment about doubting people who wrote these reviews had ever stayed in a 5* hotel. Well I've stayed at the Conrad in Chelsea Harbour, Capodimonte in Sorrento and the Four Seasons in Montreal and I would honestly say that this hotel is up there with them. When we return to Barcelona we will certainly stay at this establishment again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great on the surface! Booked very much due to the fact that i wanted a good quality hotel in a good area and the reviews seemed excellent. Hotel is in a perfect location half way up Las Ramblas. Hotel is decorated and finished to an excellent standard. The staff are NOT friendly. Must be the only hotel I've stayed at where NOBODY greets you. Rooms were very well fitted a little small but who cares, heating was always on making it very warm, but the windows open which is ok. You hear the water coming down the soil pipe whenever someone uses the shower or bathroom in another room, and the neighbour keeps cockrels which crow in the early am. NO CONCIERGE or BELLBOY, but again not too important. All in all would stay there again due to location and general fittings, but nothing else.

<Author>SBH55
<Content>Over Rated! This is a nice hotel... but really nothing special. I doubt whether those who rave about the hotel have ever stayed at a true luxury or boutique hotel. The staff is adqeuate - but impersonal. There is no extra touch that one who normally would find in a boutique hotel, nor an element of poshness/luxury that you would find in a 5 star hotel. During the stay we had issues with hot water (which were resolved quickly), and with the concierge... who seemed unable to secure a taxi no matter what the time (day or evening!).... that was truly UNACCEPTABLE. As was their attitude when I dared hale a taxi for myself... and successfully!... after they have failed for nearly 20 minutes.In summary - the services offered at the hotel are sub-par for the price. The staff is cordial, but certainly not friendly, and the hotel itself is very nice - but not amazing. Overall an adequate - but not remarkable stay.
